The Montreux Conference Will Close Tomorrow Evening and Sign the New Convention 27

Montreux The new points of the Dardanelles and Bosporus Straits have been agreed upon yesterday. The draft convention can be finalized. It is now scheduled to hold the last general meeting at 10:00 p.m. on Monday, the 19th, and sign the new convention. After the matter is completed, it will be announced to be closed. Now the Bulgarian country, which opened the conference, has also decided to sign the new convention, and does not intend to request amendments, but according to Article 16 of the convention, warships of various countries can pass through the straits to deal with aggressor countries for the implementation of regional conventions. Bulgaria argues that the so-called aggressor country should be designated by the League of Nations. (17th Havas Dispatch)

Montreux After the Montreux Conference opened today, all the demands put forward by Japan were accepted. The delegation of the country was therefore very happy and said that it was grateful that the countries participating in the conference were able to find ways to satisfy the demands put forward by Japan. The points that Japan is satisfied with are listed below:

Article 23 of the British draft originally advocated that warships of various countries may pass through the straits when implementing the covenants of the League of Nations or when implementing existing and future regional conventions, and this convention is within the structure of the League of Nations. The Japanese delegation made a reservation on this article. Now the draft of the new convention has divided the implementation of the covenants of the League of Nations and the implementation of other regional conventions into two articles. The former is included in Article 23, and the latter is included in Article 16, and a proviso is added under the wording of implementing various regional conventions, stating that this regional convention should be limited to those signed and participated by Turkey.

The draft of the new convention stipulates that submarines belonging to countries not bordering the Black Sea are not treated the same as other warships and are not allowed to pass through the straits. This is in line with Japan's requirements. Regarding this level, there is an exception, that is, submarines belonging to countries bordering the Black Sea that are built abroad or repaired abroad are treated separately.

The conference allowed Japanese training ships to freely enter and exit the straits, but their total tonnage should not exceed 15,000 tons. According to this tonnage, it is the highest limit stipulated in the draft of the new convention.

Regarding the tonnage of warships of various countries passing through the straits, according to the original agreement of the conference, the Turkish government should notify the Secretary-General of the League of Nations, Sir Eric Drummond, on a regular basis. After Japan opposed it, it was changed to notify all the signatory countries of the new convention, and Japan was also included.

The conference originally agreed that once the new convention is established, Turkey can rebuild defense fortifications on both sides of the straits. The Japanese delegation then stated that unless this issue is submitted to the Privy Council of the country for approval, the delegation will not sign any special protocol that allows Turkey to rebuild defense fortifications. This proposal has been approved by the Turkish government, so the rebuilding of defense fortifications on both sides of the straits will have to wait until the Japanese Privy Council makes a decision before it can proceed. (17th Havas)

Mutiny in Morocco, Serious Situation in Spain, Right-wing Military Officers Plotting a Coup, Government Urgently Deploys Large Troops to Suppress 28

London Today, the whole of Europe is paying attention to the events in Spanish Morocco. According to news from Gibraltar, the unrest is spreading rapidly. The Spanish government broadcast on the radio today, admitting that a rebellion had occurred in Morocco, but said that the unrest had failed. It is said that a part of the Moroccan army resisted the government. The unrest is limited to certain urban areas. No one in Spain has participated. The national army is now advancing to suppress the rebels. The authorities are capable of controlling the overall situation, and the original state will be restored soon. Although the Spanish government issued a message to appease the people, compared with other news, the situation of the unrest is increasing. (18th Reuters)

Perpignan, France An Associated Press interviewer learned today with certainty that Spanish army officers were plotting to revolt on the 25th of this month. The garrison in Melilla, Morocco, took the lead yesterday when the time was not ripe. The autonomous province of Barcelona in Spain has also been affected, but the rebellion there was put down by troops loyal to the government. One soldier died and four were injured. (18th National News)

Gibraltar An interviewer from the company recently declared that the garrison in Spanish Morocco has already rebelled, and the area is already under the control of the rebel soldiers. The Spanish government has recently dispatched a large number of infantry today, traveling by two ships, from Ceuta to Algeciras to suppress the rebellion at opportune moments. As for within Spain, there are rumors of mutiny. It is feared that it may spread throughout the country. There are also rumors that the navy stationed in the two military ports of Cartagena and Flor has mutinied. Various observers believe that the turmoil in Spain is due to the increasing infighting between the left and right political enemies after the assassination of the Royalist leader Sotelo. It is feared that the military will carry out a coup. In fact, the military has not taken any action. (18th Havas)

Paris As of 10:00 a.m. today, this place has not been able to get through to Madrid by telephone. (18th Havas)

Lisbon Since 9:00 p.m. yesterday, telephone communications between this place and Madrid have been cut off, and have not yet been restored. (18th Havas)

Madrid The mutiny in Morocco was quickly put down by the government's dispatch of troops, and it denied that there was any instability in Spain. Communications between Spain and the outside world were restored at 2:35 a.m. this morning. According to the government's announcement, the mutiny was limited to Melilla, Morocco. The claim that a revolution would occur in Spain is purely unfounded. Melilla has a total of 15,000 residents, 1,000 garrison soldiers, and a large-scale gunpowder depot. (17th National News)

保王黨領袖遇害引起重大反響　各地騷亂情形混沌 29

Madrid: Following the assassination of Royalist leader Sotelo, the situation is very tense. Cabinet members held successive cabinet meetings at the Prime Minister's office and the Ministry of Interior last night, working through the night. Moderate Socialist leader Besteiro and key party members Prieto and Cordero visited the Ministry of Interior this morning to confer with various officials. President Azaña also quickly returned to the capital from Prado. (Havas, 18th)

London: Spain is likely to experience serious riots. This morning, due to a major political event, telephone communication between the country and foreign nations was cut off. A secret telegram from Paris stated that an incident occurred in Chanca (80 miles southeast of Madrid), and the number of casualties is unknown. The current tense situation in Spain is a result of the assassination of prominent Royalist leader Sotelo on Sunday. Sotelo was taken from his residence this morning by individuals dressed as police officers, and his body was later found in the Madrid River, covered in knife and axe wounds. (Reuters, 18th)

Gibraltar: Serious disturbances have occurred in the Spanish capital Madrid and other cities such as Quintanar. Long-distance telephone communication between this port and Madrid has been cut off by Spanish authorities. Only government officials can communicate between La Línea and Madrid. Although areas bordering this port in Spain are generally calm, all troops in this port have been ordered to halt leave. (Havas, 18th)

Madrid: This morning, Spain cut off telephone communication with foreign countries, and telegrams are subject to strict censorship, causing delays of several hours compared to usual. Authorities claim this is due to political reasons. For a time, the outside world was unclear about the situation, assuming that a serious incident must have occurred in Spain. However, according to news from Hendaye, border traffic is normal.

It is reported that riots occurred in San Sebastián during the funeral of the assassinated Royalist leader Sotelo today. As the hearse proceeded to the cemetery, someone opened fire on the crowd, killing one and injuring four. Order was restored by the police after a brief disturbance. Following the interruption of telephone communication and the censorship of telegrams, Paris was the first to receive news that an incident occurred in Chanca, 80 miles southeast of Madrid, with an unknown number of casualties. Later, news arrived that disturbances had occurred in Seville, but their nature was not mentioned. (Reuters, 18th)

Madrid: After several hours of silence, the Spanish government has now acknowledged a military rebellion in Melilla, on the northern coast of Morocco. Martial law has been declared in the area, and the garrison has occupied the entire city. According to the Spanish Minister of Transport, Colonel Ylíterra, commander of the Melilla garrison, has mutinied with his troops. The military commander stationed in Melilla has surrendered. General Motomur, commander-in-chief of the Spanish forces in Morocco, has left Ceuta to go to Melilla. It is reported that the incident is local in nature, and Motomur believes he can handle the matter and clear it up soon. Melilla was originally a settlement for criminals and had a large gunpowder depot. It was opened as a commercial port in 1902. In 1909, troops were sent to suppress disturbances in nearby mines. (Reuters, 18th)

Paris: News received here from Tangier, French Morocco, indicates that serious clashes have occurred between the military and civilians in Larache. The city is an important seaport in Spanish Morocco, about 45 miles from Tangier. It is claimed that a military rebellion has occurred throughout Morocco. Travelers from Tangier to French Morocco are not allowed to pass through the Moroccan border. Incidents have occurred in the cities of Azilah, Larache, and Alcazarquivir. (Reuters, 18th)

Barcelona: No disturbances or demonstrations have occurred here. Although residents feel uneasy after the authorities implemented censorship of telegrams and telephones, everything in the city is as usual. No gunfire has been heard. General González Carrasco, a retired opposition figure, has issued a manifesto advocating the declaration of a state of war, but no one has responded. The authorities in Catalonia have confiscated the manifesto, and it is expected that General González will be arrested. Military and police authorities are still able to control the situation and have not taken special measures. (Havas, 18th)

但澤問題波蘭全國示威　但澤當局限制個人自由 31

Warsaw: A nationwide demonstration was held in Poland today to protest the plans of the German National Socialist Party in Danzig. In Warsaw alone, the number of participants reached 30,000, representing 300 organizations, most of which were convened by the Socialist Party. Flags were flying everywhere, with inscriptions such as "Danzig is part of Poland," "The mouth of the Vistula River (where Danzig is located) must belong to Poland," and "We demand the strengthening of forces to ensure the safety of the lives and property of Poles in Danzig." The crowd gathered at the old town market in Warsaw, where several people gave speeches. One person criticized the National Socialist politics in Danzig with passionate words. Finally, a resolution was passed stating that if the current system of the Free City of Danzig is to be modified without increasing Polish rights, Poland will refuse it. The initiator of today's demonstration was General Dołęga-Szeligowski, president of the Polish Maritime and Colonial League, who died in a plane crash just yesterday outside the port of Danzig. The league has also petitioned the government to strengthen Poland's position in Danzig. (Havas, 17th)

Warsaw: Members of the German National Socialist Party have been actively operating in Poland recently. Fifty-four party members, all illegal elements, have been arrested in Upper Silesia in the past few days. Many party members in the province have been arrested before, and the trials were concluded in May of this year. Those arrested this time will be tried by the court in October of this year. (Havas, 17th)

Berlin: The authorities of the Free City of Danzig took a series of shocking measures today, abolishing all freedoms recognized by the current system, such as personal freedom, freedom of speech, and freedom of publication. These measures are National Socialist in nature, as seen in the ban on Jewish gatherings. Political figures believe that these actions are tantamount to abolishing the current constitution. Observers believe that the Danzig Senate may be re-elected in the near future to legally abolish the current constitution. According to the current constitution, the National Socialist Party must obtain a two-thirds majority in the Senate to discuss constitutional amendments in order to achieve the goal of reclaiming Danzig. To obtain a two-thirds majority, a re-election must be held. However, under the current liberal system, there are concerns that the necessary votes may not be obtained, hence the implementation of the aforementioned special measures. (Havas, 18th)

London: The authorities are currently conducting a thorough investigation into the attempted assassination of the King. After the police requested witnesses to the incident to testify, they have received dozens of phone calls, and people are prepared to testify at any time. The Criminal Investigation Department has dispatched specialists to answer these calls, and some have personally gone to the station to declare their willingness to be witnesses. It is expected that the post office will deliver letters describing the incident today. All reporters will be interviewed one by one to inquire about everything. Therefore, it is expected that it will take several days to draft a complete report. The assassin, McMahon, whose real name is Bennigan, is a Bachelor of Arts from Dublin University. He has lived in West London for ten years and studied botany for some time. Recently, he demanded compensation of £20,000 for wrongful arrest and wrote to the Home Secretary and the Police Commissioner about this matter. His friends consider him a madman. He considers himself a social reformer. The police station regards him as a harmless crank who worries about the times. Special police have been paying attention to this person for some time because they heard that he had a handgun. Therefore, before the incident on Thursday, they searched the area around the scene. (Reuters, 18th)

Tokyo: According to Yomiuri Shimbun, after senior officials of the Ministry of Foreign Affairs thoroughly reviewed the report of Kuwajima, director of the East Asia Bureau, on his recent travels in North China and Manchuria, they believe that the inevitable result of tolerating smuggling in North China is that, on the one hand, it has an adverse impact on the overall diplomatic relations between China and Japan, and on the other hand, it makes Japan's diplomatic position, which has been the target of international criticism since the September 18th Incident, even more difficult. 法總理籲請人民　購買政府公債　庶不致屈服於軍火商 36

Paris: After the Chamber of Deputies passed the bill on the nationalization of the arms industry, Prime Minister Blum gave a radio address, saying that we do not need these arms capitalists, and called on the people to buy the new government bonds issued by the government, saying that the government does not want these capitalists to raise funds because they export capital to avoid taxation and abandon their obligations to the country. There will be a day when the people will settle accounts with these people. They took advantage of the country's difficulties to fill the vaults of foreign banks with gold and securities. We are issuing bonds now because we do not want to succumb to the authority of these few capitalists, but want to free ourselves. (Guomin, 17th)

Paris: The government issued short-term treasury bills worth 10 billion francs on the 10th of this month, with denominations ranging from as low as 200 francs. The principal will be repaid in one year, with an interest rate of 4%, prepaid by the government. Bondholders can request discounts from banks at any time and are exempt from income tax. The purpose is to allow funds hoarded by the public to continue to circulate in the market. Prime Minister Léon Blum gave a radio address to the nation, explaining the purpose of this treasury bill issuance, saying, "Since the people have entrusted the government with heavy responsibilities, the people should not refuse to give the government the ability it needs to fulfill its responsibilities. The issuance of the current treasury bills is a cooperative act between the government and its clients, especially small and medium-sized depositors in banks. It is highly democratic in nature and can be popularized throughout the country. The funds raised are not for the government's daily expenses, but for the implementation of the political program. This political program is what the national electorate supports. The French people do not have two personalities. It is not true that the people are ideologically revolutionary, but conservative in financial matters. What kind of sacrifice does the government seek from the people? If we talk about the way to use money, what is more appropriate and reliable than relying on national solidarity and contributing to national prosperity? The entire policy of the People's Front cabinet is to make hoarded funds circulate again in the market in order to revive the national economy. Since taking office, various measures have been tried and tested. Shouldn't the people of the country feel interested in this experience? Although there are unscrupulous people who evade taxes, the government does not want to humbly beg them to comply. What the government wants to strive for is to prevent these people from transporting bonds or cash abroad to fill the vaults of foreign banks. France has its own place to store money, and that is France itself. The government will never declare surrender to these unscrupulous people. I call out loudly to the people of the country, so that everyone can hear and unite. The treasury bills issued now are not the result of succumbing to capitalism and oligarchy, but a tool to liberate the shackles of capitalists. It is hoped that the people who love freedom will understand this meaning. I cannot help but expect it." (Havas, 17th)

Chicago: The muggy heat in the Midwest has just subsided, and now there is talk of another heat wave. Locarno Pact Conference: Britain Seeks to Resolve European Situation, Believing Tripartite Meeting of Britain, France, and Belgium Inadequate; France Also Unwilling to Declare Negotiations with Germany a Failure 39

London – Although the British government has not yet received official notification of the decision made in Paris yesterday to hold a conference of the Locarno Pact nations (Britain, Russia, Belgium) in London on July 23rd, local figures believe that the meeting cannot surpass existing diplomatic channels. London hopes that the tripartite meeting will serve to exchange opinions on issues to be discussed at a future conference of Britain, France, Belgium, Italy, and Germany. It is said that Britain wishes to participate in the meeting with broad policy objectives. British policy aims to resolve European problems. Many believe the British government will strive to prevent Europe from repeating the events of twenty-two years ago, dividing into opposing groups forming a complex situation. (Reuters, 18th)

London – Well-informed sources recently declared that if the tripartite meeting of Britain, France, and Belgium can reach an agreement, then a conference of the five Locarno Pact signatory nations (Britain, France, Belgium, Italy, and Germany) will be held in Brussels on August 15th. According to responsible sources, the British government is now planning large-scale diplomatic action. This action includes the following three phases:

Preliminary Tripartite Meeting.

A conference of the five signatory nations of the Locarno Pact. Each nation will participate on an equal footing. The purpose of the conference is to establish a new mutual assistance pact for Western Europe to replace the Locarno Pact and to guarantee the security of the borders of France and Belgium.

A large-scale European conference to be held in late summer or early autumn this year to resolve the general European situation and to revise the economic, financial, and colonial clauses contained in the Treaty of Versailles, thereby avoiding the resolution of all European issues being solely initiated by Germany or according to its plans.

It is said that Sir Vansittart, Under-Secretary of State for Foreign Affairs, informed the French Ambassador, Corbin, of the above plan during a meeting this afternoon. The government's greatest concern at this time is the five-nation conference, with the tripartite meeting merely a prelude to it. Whether a conference of all European nations can be held is still uncertain. It is now known that the agenda for the tripartite meeting will include the following issues:

Procedural issues. In other words, under what conditions and in what manner should Italy and Germany be invited to hold a five-nation conference? On this point, it would be easier to resolve if Germany could provide an answer to Britain's question. However, despite reports that Germany's answer is imminent, the British side is still eagerly awaiting it.

A new system to replace the Locarno Pact. Regarding this, Britain advocates basing it on the principle of mutual assistance and abandoning the system of unilateral guarantees. Until the new system is established, the guarantees that Britain provided to France and Belgium on March 19th of this year, namely military assistance, will remain in effect, but will not be a permanent measure.

The resolution of the general European situation. Regarding this, it should only be mentioned briefly and not seriously discussed until Germany participates in the five-nation conference and expresses a clear view. Britain is now concerned that the countries of Eastern Europe will become alarmed if the resolution is limited to Western Europe alone, and therefore urgently wishes to reassure them. At the same time, it also does not want to give Italy and Germany an excuse to become even more closely aligned. Therefore, it intends to limit the scope of discussion at the tripartite meeting and strive for clarity, so as not to present Italy and Germany with a fait accompli of an agreement between Britain, France, and Belgium, but to leave room for understanding at a future five-nation conference.

When this conference convenes, the heads of government and foreign affairs officials of the three countries – British Prime Minister Baldwin, Foreign Secretary Eden, French Prime Minister Léon Blum, Foreign Minister Yvon Delbos, Belgian Prime Minister Zeeland, and Foreign Minister Janson – will all attend in person. Its importance goes without saying, but political figures particularly value the opportunity for the British and French heads of state to meet and discuss matters. (Havas, 17th)

Paris – There have been rumors that the conference of the three Locarno Pact signatory nations (Britain, France, and Belgium) would be postponed. Official circles were deeply concerned that if this were to happen, it might be misunderstood as evidence of a passive attitude and divergent opinions among these countries. Therefore, they strongly opposed such a move. The conference is now scheduled to be held in London on the 23rd of this month, and officials are quite satisfied. They declare that the tripartite meeting will surely produce good results, promote the situation in the future, and that both Britain and France now agree that Italy and Germany should be invited to participate in a five-nation conference at a later date. Ultimately other nations might also be invited. Responsible sources have also stated that France's views on the agenda and objectives of the tripartite meeting are exactly the same as Britain's. That is, the objective of the tripartite meeting is to seek a lasting solution to the European situation. Therefore, in addition to the issue of the Rhineland regime, the general European situation should be submitted for discussion. France does not intend to ask the conference to declare that negotiations with Germany have failed. Therefore, Britain's guarantee to France and Belgium on March 19th of this year, namely the implementation of military assistance measures, will also not be considered. In addition, before the conference opens, Britain, France, and Belgium may issue a joint declaration to prove that the three countries' opinions are in complete agreement. (Havas, 17th)

Rome – The Mediterranean coastal countries formed a mutual assistance pact last autumn, and Greece also joined it. According to the Stefani News Agency here, the Greek government has formally notified the Italian ambassador that Greece now considers this mutual assistance pact to be cancelled. It is reported that Greece has informed Britain of this decision. (Havas, 17th)

Brussels – Officials have formally announced that the three signatory nations of the Locarno Pact, namely Britain, France, and Belgium, will hold a conference in London on the 22nd of this month. (Havas, 18th)

Educational Broadcasting Special Issue

Secondary Education (Part 1) 52

— Professor Liao Shicheng, Guanghua University, Shanghai

The Position of Secondary Education: China has a population of 400 million, but there are only about 400,000 secondary school students (according to the Ministry of Education's 19th year statistics, there are 179,000 senior high school students and 218,000 junior high school students). On average, there is only one secondary school student for every thousand people. Since the ratio of secondary school students to population is so small, it seems that the status of secondary school students in society is not very important. However, from another perspective, most of the leaders in the country's political, military, legal, educational, industrial, journalistic, scientific, literary, and artistic circles have received secondary education. Therefore, the quality of a country's military equipment, the profit and loss of wealth, the rise and fall of politics, the prosperity and decline of industry, and the rise and fall of culture are all directly or indirectly related to secondary education. If secondary education is not developed, the basic training of the people will not be sufficient. The so-called basic training includes both the tools of knowledge and the cultivation of the spirit. For this reason, all countries attach great importance to secondary education.

The Origin of Secondary Education: It has only been a few decades since China started running new education. The schools that were first established were mostly single-stage systems, with no institutions for continued research above and no preparatory schools below. In the 23rd year of Guangxu in the Qing Dynasty, Sheng Xuanhuai founded Nanyang Public School in Shanghai and established upper and middle divisions above the outer division, starting to have a three-stage organization. The University Regulations promulgated in the 24th year of Guangxu (1898 AD) were also divided into three stages: university hall, middle school hall, and elementary school hall. This is the origin of the name of middle school in China. In Western countries, the name of middle school appeared very early. In the ancient Athens, there was a distinction between primary and secondary schools. The first school established in Athens was the elementary school. The purpose was to temper the body and mind and cultivate noble morals in citizens, so the curriculum was very simple, with only sports and music. Later, as culture gradually progressed and society became more complex, elementary education could not meet the needs of the time, so there were organizations of philosophical schools and rhetorical schools or grammar schools. The curriculum included grammar, rhetoric, debate, logic, geometry, and other subjects, which corresponded to the middle schools of later generations. By the Renaissance, Latin middle schools were established, and secondary education became widespread in European and Western countries.

The Evolution of Secondary Education: China's formal academic system began in the 28th year of Guangxu. Since that year, the system of secondary schools has undergone several changes. The first prescribed academic system required four years of middle school to graduate, but it was not implemented. In the 29th year, the Qing court ordered Sun Jiaxiao, Zhang Baixi, and Zhang Zhidong to jointly review the school regulations and issue them to the country for implementation. The academic system established at that time changed the length of middle school to five years. At the beginning of the Republic of China, the academic system was changed again, and middle school was changed back to four years. In the tenth year of the Republic of China, the National Education Federation held a meeting in Guangzhou and passed a draft of the new academic system, which was formally promulgated by the government in the eleventh year. The spirit of the new academic system focused on the middle stage. It shortened the length of elementary school and lengthened the period of secondary school, forming a 6-3-3 system - six years of elementary school, three years of junior high school, and three years of senior high school. Although this system has been revised twice by the National Education Conference, it has remained largely unchanged and is considered the longest-lasting academic system in the history of new education in China. Critics of the academic system say that the 6-3-3 system is a product of the United States and is not suitable for national conditions. In fact, the separation of junior and senior high schools is a common trend in various countries. We can cite a few examples from Eastern and Western countries:

1. England: Although England stipulates that the period under the age of fourteen is the period for compulsory education, children can participate in competitive examinations at the age of eleven or twelve and transfer to three types of secondary schools: Grammar schools, which focus on liberal arts and sciences; "Selective Modern Schools" or Central Schools, which are not vocational schools, but have practical courses in industry and commerce, and graduate in three or four years; "Modern Schools" or Senior Elementary Schools, which focus on practical courses and graduate in three years. In this experiment, British educators believe that the period from eleven to fifteen or sixteen years old is a special educational period, during which students should be fully developed according to their individual characteristics and should not receive professional training at a very young age. Therefore, Central Schools and Senior Elementary Schools actually have the nature of junior high schools. Some people even advocate adding a four-year "junior high school department" to elementary schools. The trend of promoting junior high schools is very obvious in England.

2. France: French children can also transfer to middle school-level schools after studying in elementary school for five or six years. One type is senior elementary school, which graduates in three to five years; the other type is national and public middle school, which graduates in seven years. Although senior elementary schools focus on vocational courses, students can still transfer to liberal arts schools, which is very similar to the nature of junior high schools. National and public middle schools are divided into two circles, the first circle for four years and the second circle for three years. Each circle forms a stage, which is very similar to junior and senior high schools, isn't it?

3. Germany: German children enter middle school very early. After studying in elementary school for four years, they can transfer to secondary schools. However, after the war, the trend of secondary education was to delay specialization and make the curriculum of the first few years of each middle school consistent. The "Reform Real Middle School" is an example. Therefore, six-year middle schools, such as Kealschule and middle schools (Miltelschule), in addition to the fact that the courses in the first few years are close to elementary school, actually have the nature of junior high schools. The last three years of nine-year middle schools are similar to senior high schools.

4. Italy: Italian middle schools are usually divided into two stages. The first stage is called "Ginnasio" or junior high school. The first stage of liberal arts middle schools is five years, and teacher training schools and vocational schools are four years. The second stage is called "Liceo" or senior high school. Liberal arts middle schools and teacher training schools are three years, and vocational schools and science middle schools are four years.

5. Russia: Russia stipulates that the period from eight to seventeen years old is the period for general education. These nine years of general education are called the unified labor school. The unified labor school is divided into two departments, the first department for four years for elementary education, and the second department for five years for secondary education. The second department is further divided into an early stage and a late stage, the early stage for three years, which is suitable for junior high school; the late stage for two years, which is suitable for senior high school.

6. Japan: In the current academic system, although middle schools are stipulated to be five years, they have actually been shortened to four years, becoming a disguised junior high school; higher schools are similar to senior high schools.

Judging from the situation in various countries, there are several common points that can be brought up:

All countries acknowledge that the period from eleven or twelve years old to fifteen or sixteen years old is a special educational period.

Secondary education in all countries starts at around twelve years old.

Middle schools in all countries are divided into two stages, similar to the organization of junior high schools and senior high schools.

During the junior high school period, both further education and vocational training are generally taken into account, and the distinction is not very clear.

From this point of view, the 3-3 system is not a unique product of the United States, but a common trend in various countries. After the establishment of the National Government, all stages of education have made great progress. In terms of the improvement of secondary schools, in terms of quantity, the number of secondary school students has increased from 120,000 to more than 400,000 within ten years; in terms of quality, such as revising middle school regulations, stipulating the independence of normal schools, expanding vocational education, improving middle school curricula, promulgating moral education standards, implementing military training, and piloting the joint examination system, all have had a great impact on secondary education.

Ministry of Finance Inspects and Clears Domestic Artificial Silk Piece Goods 53

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Finance previously stipulated that imported artificial silk and artificial silk piece goods should be inspected in order to prevent smuggling. However, domestic factories also manufacture artificial silk piece goods, which are not subject to inspection. Unscrupulous merchants often use smuggled imported artificial silk to make piece goods and transfer them to the interior, which hinders the effectiveness of preventing the smuggling of artificial silk. Moreover, it is not easy to identify which artificial silk piece goods are foreign goods and which are domestic goods. If domestic goods are not inspected, licensed, and sold, it will also cause difficulties for legitimate commercial transportation. In order to prevent the aforementioned malpractices, nine measures have been specifically stipulated for the inspection and clearance of artificial silk purchased by various factories and domestic piece goods woven with artificial silk or mixed with artificial silk. On the one hand, the artificial silk of various factories or the piece goods made with mixed artificial silk will be inspected in accordance with the Provisional Regulations on the Inspection and Sale of Imported Goods. On the other hand, the inventory of artificial silk purchased by various factories and the piece goods made will be cleared. In addition to submitting a report to the Executive Yuan for record, the Ministry of Finance has separately consulted relevant departments and instructed its subordinates to handle it in accordance with the instructions on the 18th. (Central News Agency, 18th)

Transfer of Liujiang Coal Mine Stalled Again After Negotiations 62

(Tianjin) Regarding the transfer of the Liujiang Coal Mine, Ishida Hisatomo, the manager of the Taiki Company, came to Tianjin again and negotiated with Fang Zhiwu, the representative of Liujiang stationed in Tianjin. The company offered to pay 330,000 yuan upon signing the contract and the remaining 330,000 yuan in three years, or replace it with coal production. Liujiang, with a mine value of more than 2.9 million yuan, has already painfully reduced the selling price by 660,000 yuan and wants to pay the cash in one lump sum. The negotiations between the two parties have therefore stalled again. Recently, the mine's motor was damaged, and water has entered the 14th and 15th lanes. Only the 12th and 13th lanes produce coal. The water distance to the main pit is only 18 feet. Repairs will cost 100,000 yuan, and the entire mine is in danger of being abandoned. (Special Dispatch, 18th)

Travelogue of Japan (4) 66

— Our Correspondent Hu Shenchi, Hu Yizang

3. Our Compatriots in Kobe

After having a good dinner, we went to the Consulate General of the Republic of China in Kobe, located in Shimoyamatedori. This Consulate General has jurisdiction over the overseas Chinese affairs in twenty-one prefectures and counties in Kansai (including the four major cities of Osaka, Nagoya, Kyoto, and Kobe) and Shikoku. The consulate building is a two-story Western-style building, with the visa office and reception room both located downstairs. When we entered, Consul General Jiang Hua was not in the consulate, so Vice Consul Pan Jinyao came out to receive us. Vice Consul Pan is a handsome young man who talked with us cordially for two hours in the reception room. He gave us much guidance regarding our travel. When we inquired about overseas Chinese affairs, he replied in detail as follows:

'The number of overseas Chinese in Kobe was originally not large, but since the Great Kanto Earthquake in the twelfth year of the Republic of China (1923), a large number of overseas Chinese from Yokohama moved here, and the number greatly increased. According to a survey by the Kobe Municipal Government in the nineteenth year of the Republic of China (1930), there were more than 6,600 people, which was the peak period for overseas Chinese in Kobe. After the Mukden Incident occurred, many overseas Chinese here returned to China, and the number greatly decreased. According to the latest register of the Consulate General, there are 1,700 households and more than 3,800 people of overseas Chinese in Kobe, most of whom are engaged in commerce or handicrafts. In terms of commerce, there are more than 70 overseas Chinese trading firms in the local area, including Fuyuhe, opened by Ma Pin San (engaged in the import and export of sugar and ramie), and Xinruixing, opened by Zhou Qibo (engaged in the export of cotton cloth and cotton yarn), which are larger in scale, each with a capital of 500,000 Japanese yen. Trading companies can be divided into two major groups: Guangdong-Fujian and Sanjiang. The Guangdong-Fujian group mostly deals in business in Southeast Asia, while the Sanjiang group mostly deals in seafood. In addition, there are 15 overseas Chinese-owned grocery stores, 9 money exchange shops, and more than 100 silk shops in Kobe. In terms of handicrafts, there are mostly tailors, barbers, chefs, and painters. There are 56 tailor shops, 62 barber shops, 13 restaurants, and 8 painting workshops in Kobe, all of which are opened by overseas Chinese.

'In order to relieve unemployment in their own country, the Japanese government has been tightening its restrictions on Chinese laborers year after year. Now, not only are there no Chinese workers in factories all over Japan, but even the overseas Chinese who were originally engaged in handicrafts in Japan, such as barbers, tailors, and chefs, are still subject to strict restrictions by the Japanese police at any time. Since the thirty-second year of Meiji (1899), the Japanese government has promulgated several laws and regulations to restrict foreign labor and foreign entry. (Note) Any newly arrived Chinese who want to live in Japan must have a guarantor to ensure that they will not engage in labor in Japan before they can disembark. Existing overseas Chinese barbers and chefs must obtain passports from the authorities, which must be renewed every year. If the authorities suspend the issuance of passports, they will have to close their businesses.'

'Last year, a dispute over the suppression of Chinese workers occurred in Nagoya. Consul General Jiang personally went there to investigate. That group of Chinese workers did not obtain permission from the authorities, but was secretly hired by a Japanese foreman to do the hard work of transporting coal. Originally, Japanese foremen liked to hire Chinese laborers because they could endure more hardship than Japanese workers. Although they were subjected to harsh treatment and only earned 30 or 40 cents a day, they could still save money to send back to their home country. However, since that dispute occurred, there have been no more Chinese laborers in Nagoya.'

When we asked about the organizations and schools of overseas Chinese in Kobe, Vice Consul Pan replied: 'There is a Kobe-Osaka Chinese Association, which has a long history and is similar in nature to the charitable halls in the mainland, handling the charitable affairs of overseas Chinese. The association's building was built with funds raised by overseas Chinese. The annual expenses are covered by the rent from the association's leased real estate (3,000 yuan per year), and donations are solicited from local overseas Chinese merchants at any time. A few years ago, when China suffered a major flood, the Chinese Association remitted a large amount of donations to the country, which shows the concern of the overseas Chinese in Kobe for their motherland. Currently, there are 23 directors of the association, and one person is publicly elected as the chairman, who is usually rotated among the Guangdong, Fujian, and Sanjiang groups. In addition, there are also the Kobe Guangye Guild, the Kobe Sanjiang Chamber of Commerce, the Kobe Fujian Chamber of Commerce, the Kobe Chinese Merchants' Nanyang Export Association, the Kobe Chinese Tailors' Association, the Kobe Chinese Barbers' Association, the Kobe Chinese Painting Industry Association (i.e., the Painters' Union), the Hyogo Prefecture Chinese Silk Industry Association, the Kobe Anhui-Jiangxi League, the Kobe Chinese Chefs' Association, and the Kobe Chinese Charity Association. As for the schools run by overseas Chinese, there are currently only two primary schools. The Kobe Chinese Tongwen School was closed for a year due to the September 18th Incident. It is divided into two departments: primary school and kindergarten. There are currently 14 faculty members and more than 400 students. The principal is Mr. Zheng Hanguang. The Kobe-Osaka Chinese Primary School is managed by the Sanjiang Guild, with 7 teachers and more than 200 students. The principal is Mr. Dong Gongxu.'

Vice Consul Pan also talked about Kobe's trade with China: 'According to the consulate's visa manifest, the goods shipped from Kobe to China every month total more than 2 million Japanese yen, of which more than 1 million are exported to Shanghai. The main types of goods are cotton yarn, seafood, and textiles.' Of course, in reality, Kobe's exports to China are far more than this amount, because the so-called special trade that evades our country's customs duties is developing day by day.

(Note) Excerpts from various Japanese laws and regulations restricting foreign labor and foreign entry are as follows:

(1) Regarding Foreigners' Residence and Business

(Japanese Imperial Ordinance No. 352, July 28, Meiji 32 (1899))

Article 1: Although foreigners do not have the freedom to reside according to treaties or customs, they may move and do business outside the former settlements and mixed residences. However, those engaged in labor may not reside or engage in business outside the former settlements and mixed residences without the permission of the administrative authorities.

The types of labor and the detailed rules for the implementation of this ordinance shall be determined by the Minister of Interior.

Article 2: Those who violate the provisions of the proviso in paragraph 1 of the preceding article shall be fined no more than 100 yen.

Article 3: This ordinance shall be implemented from August 4, Meiji 32 (1899).

Article 4: Ordinance No. 0 of Meiji 27 (1894) shall be repealed from the date of implementation of this ordinance.

(2) Detailed Rules for the Implementation of Matters Regarding Foreigners' Residence and Business

(Japanese Ministry of Interior Ordinance No. 42, July 28, Meiji 32 (1899))

Article 1: The administrative authorities referred to in Article 1 of the ordinance refer to the governors of prefectures and counties.

Article 2: The term "laborers" in Article 1 of the Imperial Ordinance refers to those engaged in labor such as agriculture, fishing, mining, civil engineering, construction, manufacturing, transportation, cart pulling, manual labor, and other miscellaneous services; however, domestic employees or cooks are not included in this category.

Article 3: The governors of prefectures and counties may revoke the permission for laborers if they deem it necessary for the public interest.

(3) Measures for the Suppression of Qing Chinese Laborers

(Japanese Ministry of Interior Instruction No. 20, August, Meiji 32 (1899))

(Omitted) The above-mentioned Imperial Ordinance and Instruction aim to suppress Qing Chinese laborers because they not only pose a risk of disrupting customs but also cause disputes with Japanese labor competition and hinder public order. Therefore, Qing Chinese laborers corresponding to Article 2 of the Ministry Ordinance, except for those engaged in miscellaneous services, shall not reside or engage in labor outside the former settlements and mixed residences. (Omitted)

(4) Regarding Foreigners' Entry into the Country

(Japanese Ministry of Interior Ordinance No. 1, January 24, Taisho 7 (1918))

Article 1: The local governor may prohibit the landing of foreigners who come to Japan and are deemed to correspond to one of the following items. (Paragraph 1)

(1) Those who do not have a passport or nationality certificate.

(2) Those whose actions are contrary to the interests of Japan or who intend to benefit enemy countries.

(3) Those who pose a risk of disturbing public order or disrupting customs.

(4) Those who have a habit of vagrancy or begging.

(5) Those who are infected with various infectious diseases or other diseases that endanger public health.

(6) Those who are mentally deranged, mentally weak, impoverished, or otherwise in need of assistance. (Paragraph 2 omitted)

Article 2: The provisions of item 1 of paragraph 1 of the preceding article may not be applied to citizens of countries whose Japanese citizens do not require a passport or nationality certificate to enter.

Article 3: Foreigners who come to Japan shall make a truthful statement when questioned by the police officer about the matters in each item of paragraph 1 of Article 1 and other necessary matters. (This article is a summary translation)

Article 4: Those who violate the provisions of the preceding article may be prohibited from landing or ordered to leave the territory of Japan. (This article is a summary translation)

(5) Form for Guarantee of Chinese Landing

(Hyogo Prefecture Foreign Affairs Section, March, Taisho 13 (1924))

Guarantee

Name Age (of the person coming to Japan) from a certain county in a certain province of China.

The above-mentioned so-and-so arrived here today on the so-and-so ship and is prohibited from landing. However, this person is an employee of the guarantor's store and was instructed to come here. In the future, not only will they not be allowed to engage in labor, but the guarantor is willing to abide by the following articles, and I earnestly request permission for them to land.

Detailed as follows:

(1) The guarantee shall not engage in labor.

(2) The guarantee shall only be employed by the employer at the time of landing and shall not work elsewhere.

(3) The employment of the guarantee shall not result in the dismissal of persons previously employed for the same purpose.

(4) If the guarantee is dismissed or wishes to change their service, they shall immediately report to the police station and the Kobe Maritime Police Department under its jurisdiction and order them to return to their country, unless prior permission is obtained from the Hyogo Prefectural Office. However, the guarantor shall be responsible for the cost of repatriation and all debts incurred.

(5) If the guarantee flees, dies, or their whereabouts are unknown, the guarantor shall report it to the police station in charge within five days.

(6) If there is any change in the guarantee's address, name, or nationality, the guarantor shall immediately report it to the police station in charge.

(7) When the authorities request the guarantor to pay for the guarantee's travel expenses and other expenses, the guarantor shall immediately be responsible for them and immediately order them to return to their country.

(8) If the guarantee is ill or requires other assistance, the guarantor shall provide appropriate assistance. If the guarantee requires protection or investigation by the authorities in Japan, the guarantor shall be responsible for all expenses, whether the guarantor agrees or not.

Miscellaneous Writings on Rural Hubei 69

— Special Correspondent Cheng Jun

(21) Rural Scenes in Zhongxiang After the Disaster

Zhongxiang borders the Han River and is rich in rice and cotton, making it the essence of agriculture in the province. Recently, due to the collapse of the Yaodi Dike, it has suffered another flood disaster. The melon of Huangtai has been picked again and again. The countryside is desolate, and it has become the same as other counties. After the reporter inspected the Yaodi Dike, he conducted a survey of the rural areas of the entire county. Seeing that the past glory has become a thing of the past and thinking of the difficulty of recovery and the ease of destruction, I couldn't help but feel emotional.

The county is divided into three townships: mountain, lake, and river. The fields in the mountain township are alternately fertile and barren, suitable for growing rice and wheat. The lake and river townships, except for low-lying and sandy areas, are all fertile land, suitable for growing sesame, cotton, soybeans, ramie, sorghum, etc. The rice in the mountain township is the most abundant, reaching more than 2 million dan per year, which is transported in large quantities out of the country, either from Yangzikou and out of Chihekou, or from Bengtoukang and out of Lihekou, to reach the Xiang River, all of which are extremely convenient. Fengle River, Huangzhuangmiao, and Tanggang are also ports for transporting rice out of the country. After the autumn harvest, sailing boats are like weaving, with 60-70% transporting rice and the rest transporting cotton and sesame. The countryside is a purely agricultural society, and farmers mainly engage in farming and do not engage in animal husbandry, fishing, or hunting. Therefore, the resources for their livelihood all depend on the income from agricultural products. In recent years, they have often had good harvests, and their lives have been relatively stable. The taxes they bear are 1.2 cents of regular tax per mu of high-quality land, 7 cents of surtax, 1 dime of mu donation, and 5 cents of baojia fee, totaling 3.6 cents. For medium-quality land, it is 8 cents of regular tax per mu, 6 cents of surtax, 1 dime of mu donation, and 5 cents of baojia fee, totaling 2.9 cents. For low-quality land, it is 6 cents of regular tax per mu, 4 cents of surtax, 1 dime of mu donation, and 5 cents of baojia fee, totaling 2.5 cents. The amount of tax is also quite fair, depending on the fertility of the land. Farmers work at sunrise and rest at sunset, and their hard work is enough to provide them with food and clothing. In the environment of widespread rural bankruptcy, they are surprisingly self-sufficient, which is due to the fertility of the land.

The abundant agricultural production is due to the fertile land and convenient irrigation. However, because it borders the Han River, it is prone to floods. Fortunately, there is a large dike to provide protection. Unexpectedly, last autumn's flood, the collapse of the Xiang Dike, was in Zhongxiang territory, with a total of 18 breaches in the Third and Fourth sections of construction, as well as the Eleventh section of construction. Three breaches occurred in the protective city dike, and the people's dike in the central and northern sections also completely collapsed. The Han River carried the momentum of a waterfall and drove straight down, and the devastation was unprecedented, breaking all previous records. The flooded area was more than 11.4 million li, accounting for 24% of the national area. The flooded farmland was 706,370 mu, accounting for 50%. The sandy land was 223,310 mu, and 50,114 houses were washed away. The population death toll was 220,822, and the number of disaster victims was 318,320. The loss of agricultural products and livestock is even more difficult to estimate. After this unprecedented catastrophe, the vitality was depleted, and bandits such as Qiu Zhaigong, Mei Daoxian, and Xiang Youyao took the opportunity to stir up trouble. The team of Song Dewen and others then mutinied. Starving people and hooligans colluded to intercept ships, creating a chaotic situation. Although County Magistrate Xiong Daochen quelled the rebellion, and the public order was maintained, the essence of the countryside was exhausted.

This spring, the National Economic Council built a Yaodi Dike that stretched for more than 40 Chinese miles, all within the county's territory. It was originally intended to provide work relief to disaster victims. Initially, due to poor management, the disaster victims who came to work and receive relief could not even support themselves after working all day, and they fled one after another. Then, the Lianbao chiefs and baojia heads forced them to work, causing great disturbance to the people. By the time the two wheats were ripe in May, they were not allowed to harvest them because of the dike construction, and there was no time to plant new seedlings. They still thought that the dike construction would be completed and they could celebrate peace forever. Unexpectedly, on the 26th of that month, the Yaodi Dike collapsed, and the water was torrential. Tens of miles outside the dike became a vast expanse of water. Most of the area inside the dike was also flooded. The people were serving on the dike and could not spare themselves to rescue. The ripe wheat and beans were all submerged. Many of the elderly, weak, women, and children were drowned. The total disaster area was 3,000 square li, and the number of disaster-stricken households was 17,000 households and 83,000 people, which was not as great as the previous year's major disaster, but the suffering of the farmers was even greater than last year. After last year's disaster, the countryside had nothing. They did not hesitate to borrow from various sources to start spring farming. The wheat and bean seedlings were all debts of the farmers' blood. Now they have been washed away by the flood again, and no new seedlings have been planted. The autumn harvest is also hopeless. Not only will they not have the ability to borrow money for farming in the future, but they will also have no way to maintain their simple lives at present. Grass roots and tree bark have now become treasures. The county borders Suizao, and bandits appear and disappear unpredictably. Now that they have suffered another catastrophe, the honest farmers will eventually take risks. This is what discerning people are deeply concerned about. (Sent from Zhongxiang)

Page 10

Japanese Warships Freely Enter and Exit Shantou Port Japanese Warships Regularly Cruise the Coasts of Fujian and Guangdong Will Use the Pretext of Protecting Overseas Chinese to Wait for an Opportunity to Act 70

Shantou Correspondence Lieutenant Commander Nishioka Shigetai, Commander of the 13th Destroyer Squadron of the Japanese Navy in Taiwan, arrived in Shantou on the 30th of last month with the warships "Uzutake" and "Hazutake." The municipal government was not notified in advance, and they sailed into the harbor and docked. Nishioka met with Mayor Chen Tongchang and East District Committee Member Li Hanhun on the 20th of this month, raised the "Kakuda Incident," and attached many conditions, demanding that Li agree to resolve them. Later, Li resigned and left Shantou. Nishioka then led the "Uzutake" and "Hazutake" warships back to Xiamen to report the negotiation process to Hosogaya, Commander of the 16th Fleet of the Japanese Navy. Hosogaya, as the representative of the Taiwan Governor-General's Office, is responsible for negotiating the case, while the Japanese Consul in Shantou is only assisting. On the 8th, Nishioka again led the "Uzutake" and "Hazutake" warships to Shantou, still without notifying the municipal government in advance. They freely enter and exit Shantou Port. However, on the 9th, the two warships returned to Xiamen. Currently, Japanese warships cruising along the coasts of Fujian and Guangdong include "Asagao," "Fuyou," "Kanzou," and "Hayanae." They often travel back and forth in the coastal waters. Smuggling steamers and sailing boats, loaded with large quantities of smuggled goods from Taiwan or the Fujian border, often follow Japanese warships to Nanao to unload their cargo. At the coastal areas of Nanao, Ronin groups have set up 13 warehouses. Seamen and inferior people are often in secret collusion with smugglers to unload smuggled goods and transport them to the Chaoshan and Meizhou inland for sale. Currently, Chaoshan only has 100 men from the 17th Gendarmerie Brigade, 300 men from the Public Security Bureau's Security Brigade, 800 policemen from various districts, and over 400 anti-smuggling soldiers, distributed in various locations to maintain public order. National defense is extremely weak. According to rumors, the Japanese fleet is waiting for an opportunity to act in Xiamen. Moreover, the Japanese side has lodged three protests due to the "Kakuda Incident" and Chen Jitang's anti-Japanese stance. Furthermore, according to information leaked by Taiwanese people in Shantou, if a war breaks out in the upper reaches of the Han River or on the Fujian border, Japanese warships will definitely send sailors ashore under the pretext of protecting overseas Chinese to reap the benefits. Therefore, the general public in Chaoshan is both afraid of war between Yu Hanmou's army and Chen Jitang's army and worried that foreign powers will take advantage of the situation to invade, endangering the territory. Therefore, they are all deeply worried.

Shanghai-Hankou Three-Route Water-Land Joint Transport - Implemented on July 21st - 71

Wuhu Correspondence: In the past, the Yangtze River shipping between Shanghai and Hankou was dominated by Chinese and foreign merchants. Goods were monopolized by them, and travelers rarely transferred by train via Nanjing. In recent years, due to the impact of rising and falling water levels, all upstream and downstream goods are transshipped through Wuhu every winter. This is because Wuhu is located in the middle of Shanghai and Hankou, controlling the intersection of upstream and downstream. Since the completion of the Jingwu section of the Jiangnan Railway Company and the joint track with the Yaohuamen station in Nanjing, and the joint transport of cars with the Beijing-Shanghai Railway, the traffic in the lower reaches of the Yangtze River has changed. Although the freight transport of the Huainan Road to the Beijing-Shanghai Railway is limited to four kinds of wheat, rice, rapeseed, and soybeans, the export of agricultural products from Anhui Province is very different from the past. The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company believed that it was necessary to cooperate with the Jiangnan Road and the Beijing-Shanghai Railway in the lower reaches to carry out joint water-land transport. After several discussions, detailed measures have been planned. The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company specially sent Zeng Guangqing, the chief of the Business Department, and the Beijing-Shanghai and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railways specially sent Xiao Weiguo, the chief of the Train Department, to Wuhu on the 16th to sign a contract with Zhou Xiansong, the general manager and transport director of the Jiangnan Road. It was decided to implement it from July 21st and try it for six months. The Jiangnan Road will also increase the speed of the Jingwu section trains by 40 minutes from July 21st. In the future, the situation of water and land transportation on the Yangtze River will change greatly.

The Beijing-Shanghai Railway Joint Transport Stations include Shanghai, Suzhou, Wuxi, and Zhenjiang. The Jiangnan Road Joint Transport Stations are Nanjing Zhonghuamen, Dangtu, Wuhu, and Xuancheng. The China Merchants Steam Navigation Company Joint Transport Stations are Datong, Anqing, Jiujiang, Wuxue, and Hankou, all with Wuhu as the connecting station. In terms of time, in addition to the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company ships still operating on schedule, strive for accurate time. (1) The Shanghai-Wuhu direct train departs from Shanghai at 7:55 and Nanjing at 14:40, arriving in Wuhu at 17:30, connecting with the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company upstream ship. It departs from Wuhu at 8:00, connecting with the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company downstream ship, arriving in Nanjing at 11:00 and Shanghai at 20:50. (2) Jiangnan Road Wuhu-Sunjiafu section: departs from Wuhu at 11:00 and arrives in Sunjiafu at 14:00. (3) Beijing-Wuhu direct train departs from Nanjing at 11:50 and arrives in Wuhu at 14:55. Also, it departs from Nanjing at 18:50 and arrives in Wuhu at 31:50. It departs from Wuhu at 10:45 and arrives in Nanjing at 12:55. Also, it departs from Wuhu at 13:10 and arrives in Nanjing at 16:06.

The freight rates are all charged at 85% of the original price. The passenger joint tickets are also reduced to the lowest discount. (1) From the Beijing-Shanghai Railway with Nanjing as the central station, the third-class train fare is 2.55 yuan from Shanghai North Station for the ordinary train and 3 yuan for the express train. From Wuxi, the fare is 1.65 yuan for the ordinary train and 1.95 yuan for the express train. From Zhenjiang, the fare is 6 yuan for the ordinary train and 7 yuan for the express train. (2) From the central station Nanjing to Wuhu via the Jiangnan Road, the fare is 1.45 yuan from Zhonghuamen, 1.15 yuan from Yaohuamen, 4 yuan from Dangtu, and 0.85 yuan from Xuancheng. (3) For those who come to Wuhu from the upper reaches of the Yangtze River by China Merchants Steam Navigation Company first-class ship, the fare is 0.75 yuan from Datong, 1.2 yuan from Anqing, 2.25 yuan from Jiujiang, 2.55 yuan from Wuxue, and 3.45 yuan from Hankou. (16th)

Serious Disaster in Hexi, Gansu Province: Provincial Government Distributes Relief Funds and Orders Counties to Lift Grain Restrictions 72

Lanzhou Correspondence: Yu Xuezhong, Chairman of the Gansu Provincial Government, previously stated that various counties in the province had suffered successive natural and man-made disasters, leading to rural bankruptcy and people unable to make a living. The situation was especially dire in the counties of the Western Route [Hexi Corridor]. To provide relief and prevent widespread suffering, he requested and received approval from the Central Government for the allocation of 250,000 yuan in public bonds, equivalent to 147,273.70 yuan in cash, for disaster relief. However, given the severity of the disaster in the Hexi counties, it was decided to allocate over 78,000 yuan first, distributing it according to the varying degrees of disaster in each Hexi county, to meet immediate relief needs. This proposal has already been submitted to the Provincial Affairs Conference, which resolved to allocate the relief funds according to the proposed distribution amounts. It is reported that the provincial government, to ensure that the disaster victims receive practical assistance as soon as possible to sustain their lives, wired the allocated relief funds to various sub-bureaus in Hexi through the Ping City Official Money Bureau a few days ago, instructing the respective county magistrates to collect the funds and distribute them earnestly and diligently. As for the remaining portion of the public bonds, after allocating funds to the Hexi counties, there is a remaining balance of over 60,000 yuan. This has been further allocated: 2,000 yuan to the Provincial Capital Public Security Bureau for relief of refugees, and 2,000 yuan to Commissioner Hu of the three districts in eastern Gansu to handle local post-disaster affairs. The provincial government originally intended to allocate the remaining funds to other disaster-stricken counties after receiving reports from all affected areas, and would then distribute the funds evenly. However, because the counties that have already reported disasters are in urgent need of relief, the provincial government, to expedite relief efforts, has decided to first select the counties with the most severe disasters from those that have already submitted reports and distribute funds to them in advance for relief. The remainder will be distributed after all reports have been received, to avoid delaying relief work. This demonstrates the provincial government's concern for the disaster situation.

Regarding the disaster situation in the Hexi counties, according to reliable investigations, the most severely affected are Jiuquan, Anxi, Yumen, and Dunhuang. Recently, the number of disaster victims in Jiuquan City alone has exceeded 4,000. Although the government provides each person with four taels of cooked noodles daily as relief, this is insufficient due to the large number of people and the limited amount of noodles. There have been reports of disaster victims starving to death. In May, the county governments implemented a ban on grain exports, and wealthy households also hoarded food and refused to sell it. Upon hearing this, the Commissioner's Office urgently ordered all counties to immediately issue a proclamation lifting the grain export ban, and instructed wealthy households in both urban and rural areas to open up their granaries and sell grain fairly, without engaging in price gouging. After the order was issued, secret agents were dispatched to various counties to investigate whether there was any insincere compliance. As a result, current grain prices have fallen slightly compared to early June.

The Truth About the Fishermen's Riot on Daishan Island—Triggered by Increased Salt Taxes 73

Ningbo Correspondence: On the afternoon of the 13th, fishermen and salt workers on Daishan Island, Dinghai, clashed with tax police over opposition to "return piling" [a salt tax collection method], setting fire to the weighing station and the office of the salt field administration, and killing Miao Guang, the director of the Daishan field and head of the weighing station, Qian Dianhe, an employee, and Hu Bugui, the tax police captain. Many fishermen and salt workers were also killed or injured. It is reported that the real cause of the incident was the increase in salt taxes. In previous years, fishermen purchasing salt for fishing were charged four yuan per salt permit. Each boat household was allowed to purchase one permit, which entitled them to purchase a season's worth of fishing salt without additional fees. This year, there was an attempt to increase the tax on permits, with each salt permit only allowing the purchase of ten dan of salt, approximately 1,300 jin, costing four yuan. However, each fishing boat typically requires 7,000 to 8,000 jin of salt per season, and even more for larger boats. Therefore, each boat would have to pay at least 20 yuan in permit fees per season. Furthermore, if the fish catch was small and there was leftover fishing salt, it would have to be weighed and taxed at the weighing station, otherwise, if discovered by tax inspectors, it would be treated as smuggled salt and punished. As a result, many were subjected to tax inspections and penalties, leading to deep resentment. Also, the office hours of the weighing station were set from 8:00 a.m. to 4:00 p.m., after which salt weighing would cease. Therefore, fishing boats arriving at night or in the middle of the night wanting to purchase fishing salt would have to wait until the next day. The fishermen's fishing season only lasts for three "big tides" each month, and often waiting to purchase fishing salt would delay one tide, resulting in significant losses. This is a major reason for the fishermen's hatred of the weighing station. According to visitors from Daishan, the number of weighing station staff killed in this incident, excluding the director Miao Guang, totaled more than 20. The number of tax police killed or injured could not be accurately determined. More than 30 fishermen and salt workers were killed, and over 100 were injured. The most gruesome aspect was that the hearts of the murdered weighing station staff and tax police were gouged out by the fishermen. It is said that the people of Daishan always resort to this cruel method when causing trouble, believing that extracting a person's heart and liver can cure heart pain. Currently, the provincial authorities have dispatched security teams, water police, and tax police to suppress the situation and apprehend the perpetrators for punishment. However, the rioters have fled en masse after the incident. Shops, however, have resumed business as the situation has calmed down.

Reorganization of Zhang Kewu's Bandit Troops in Southern Fujian; Recruitment of Lu Zhenshan's Troops Also Planned; Zhang and Lu's Troops are the Largest in Southern Fujian 74

Xiamen Correspondence: Zhang Kewu's bandit troops in Dehua were reorganized by Ye Cheng, Deputy Director of the Security Department, on the 13th in Nanting, Dehua. Seven companies were formed and issued 3,000 yuan for food expenses. Ye returned to Dehua County that evening, passed through Quanzhou on the 14th, and arrived in Xiamen on the morning of the 15th. According to Ye, "I arrived in Dehua on the 12th and went to the Nanting Shiniushan area where Zhang's troops were gathering. I personally inspected Zhang's troops with Huang Su, the commander of the 2nd Security Regiment, Councilor Zhu Zhaohang, clerks Jiang and Liu, and a mobile soldier. Zhang's troops had concentrated five companies, five to six hundred men, with weapons including automatic rifles, machine guns, pistols, and rifles. Another unit of over two hundred men had not arrived due to the rain. It is estimated that those arrived and not arrived in Dehua have seven companies, and another unit is concentrated in Xianyou due to the long distance. Councilor Zhu and clerks Jiang and Liu were left to handle the unfinished reorganization work. I passed through Quanzhou to Xiamen and plan to report the progress to Director Jiang in Zhangzhou tomorrow (the 16th). After Zhang's troops are reorganized, they will be under the Security Department as security teams, and a regiment or several battalions may be established in the future. The selection of officers and their designations will be determined after the reorganization is completed. Zhang Kewu said that he was originally a small businessman and does not want to take on heavy responsibilities again, and intends to invite Zhang Xiongnan, who is currently in Hong Kong, to return and preside over the troops. As for Lu Zhenshan's bandits in Anxi, they are fewer in number than Zhang's troops. It is reported that Lu and Zhang are also in alliance, and it is planned to recruit them first and reorganize them into regular security teams. If Lu remains stubborn, the 2nd and 9th Security Regiments stationed in Quanzhou and Yongchun will be ordered to encircle and suppress them. With the Lu troops resolved, the bandit problem in southern Fujian can be declared settled." It is reported that Zhang Kewu's troops are the largest in southern Fujian and are also a relatively strong civilian army. They were originally Zhang Xiongnan's troops, and after Zhang Xiongnan left the army, Zhang Kewu took over leading his troops. Lu Zhenshan is a major bandit leader, but his troops are smaller than Zhang's, and his strength is far inferior. If the recruitment and reorganization of the two troops is successful, the problem of the civilian army in southern Fujian can be completely resolved. Currently, the Security Department has sent Lin Qianzheng to contact Lu. (July 16th)

Survey of Shipping in Qingdao: Japanese Ships are the Most Numerous in Passenger and Cargo Transport, Followed by Chinese and Then British 75

Qingdao Correspondence: Since Qingdao was returned to our country, active construction has been underway. Recently, a shipyard and the No. 3 Wharf have been established. Ships of 10,000 tons or more can be docked for repairs at any time and can be loaded and unloaded near the wharf. The facilities are complete, so commerce is developing rapidly and the number of imported ships is increasing daily. In addition to the irregular arrivals and departures of Japanese warships, during the summer, dozens of European and American warships, cruisers and destroyers, visit the port for summering. As for passenger and cargo ships arriving at the port, Japanese ships are the most numerous, with 732 ships annually, totaling 1,346,342 tons. Cargo ships account for 40% and scheduled passenger and cargo ships account for 60%. Chinese ships are the second most numerous, with 626 ships annually, totaling 711,856 tons. Cargo ships account for 80% and scheduled passenger and cargo ships account for 20%. British ships are the next most numerous, with 528 ships annually. Cargo ships account for 80% and passenger and cargo ships account for 20%. This is just a statistical overview of the recent situation. A review of the total number of Chinese and foreign passenger and cargo ships entering and leaving the port annually and their total tonnage is as follows: China: 626 ships, 711,856 tons; Japan: 732 ships, 1,346,342 tons; England: 528 ships, 995,748 tons; Norway: 66 ships, 135,529 tons; America: 35 ships, 147,273 tons; Germany: 35 ships, 196,158 tons; Denmark: 41 ships, 82,557 tons; Italy: 11 ships, 37,761 tons; Greece: 2 ships, 6,301 tons; Switzerland: 1 ship, 3,834 tons. The tonnages listed above are all registered tonnages. The ships referred to are ocean-going vessels. Small steamers sailing inland or in Jiaozhou Bay are not included.

Robbery Case in the Eastern Suburbs of Songjiang 76

Landlord Yang Pingyu Commits Suicide in Suzhou 77

Yang Pingyu, 34 years old, residing at No. 52 Dongmatazi Lane, Lindun Road, Suzhou City, owned over 2,000 mu of fertile land and lived a very prosperous life. Recently, due to the peasants' resistance to rent and the establishment of public depots in various districts, Yang also appointed his bookkeeper Zhu Peichu to join the sixth district public depot in Weijingtang to collect arrears of rent. Since the tragic rent collection incident in Weijingtang, the families of peasants such as Gu Zian, who were shot and killed by the security team, have hired lawyers and formally filed a lawsuit with the local court, and published a warning in the newspaper. Yang, suffering from palpitations, developed the idea of ​​fearing punishment and being tired of the world, and hanged himself the night before (the 17th). Because he was sleeping alone in a room, no one noticed at first. Previously, Feng Runzhen, a rent collection committee member in the case, had a bedding roll placed in Yang's bedroom. It was not until yesterday morning (the 18th) when Feng instructed someone to go and move the bedding that Yang's death was discovered. Yang's wife, Wu, then petitioned the court for exemption from inspection.

Additionally, Yang graduated from Yancheng High School, and his wife, Huang, studied at Datong University in Shanghai. They had two sons, the eldest being only 14 years old. It is estimated that they had 400 mu of land in Weijingtang, on which their livelihood depended entirely. Last year, the average rent collected per mu was only one yuan, while the land tax to be paid was one yuan and two jiao per mu. Yang was physically weak and suffered from neurasthenia. This suicide is suspected to have been caused by panic. The day before (the 17th) in the afternoon, he went to the Jiuru Teahouse for a drink. After returning, he washed his feet and went to sleep upstairs, while his wife and children lived downstairs. Yesterday morning (the 18th), someone went to inquire about the address of Feng Runzhen, only to discover that Yang had hanged himself. It was learned that Yang was disappointed about the rent collection, and had set up a summer tutoring center at home this summer, teaching 20 male and female students, with his wife as an assistant teacher, to supplement their income. It can also be seen from this that his situation was not as good as before. It is also learned that his father was also a neurotic person in his lifetime, so Yang's suicide seems to be related to heredity.

Suzhou-Wuxi Highway to be Completed Soon 78
