River Rises Five Feet in Wuxi 79

Since the beginning of summer, the weather has been uneven, suddenly cold and suddenly hot, coupled with torrential rain, continuous all day long, resulting in the river rising sharply, measuring as much as five feet. Low-lying fields are in danger of being submerged. Farmers are generally planning for flood prevention work. Small boats in the countryside are also facing difficult navigation due to the river being full. Some bridge openings and decks are only about two feet away from the water, so it is difficult for small boats to pass. If the river rises another two inches, there is a risk of suspension of navigation.

Cruelty of Roadside Robbery in Yangzhou 81

Wang Yuhai, a farmer from Yaowan, Ganquan Mountain, in the western countryside of Jiangdu, was carrying a load of baskets to Dongge outside Yangzhou to buy sweet potato seedlings at about 3:00 a.m. on the 14th. Yu and the other six still refused to let Wang go, so Shi left. Sea Wall Sand Accretion Collapses in Hangzhou 83

The sand outside the sea wall in western Zhejiang, from Haidu Eight Forts to Jiuli Bridge, has seen new sand accretion of about 10 kilometers long and more than 5 kilometers wide since last year. The Finance Department sent staff to investigate, intending to allow the people to claim and cultivate it after a considerable period of time, and to pay taxes. However, the spring tide this year was particularly large, and all the accumulated sand has been completely collapsed by the huge waves. The water is approaching the embankment, and the embankment is turning dangerous. The Water Conservancy Engineering Department of the Construction Department has been notified and has sent personnel to measure the shape of the riverbed in order to plan for the prevention of danger.

Debt Collection Leads to Murder in Pinghu 85

The Daishengchang Rice Shop in this city went bankrupt due to poor business. The shareholders were repaid at a rate of 50 per thousand, but Qian Bingyan, a wealthy household, was owed more than a thousand yuan, which was supposed to be repaid at 200 per thousand. Qian refused and went to urge the payment repeatedly without success. Yesterday, Tang Yangmin, the manager of the rice shop, was recuperating from an illness in a room inside Daishengchang when several bailiffs suddenly arrived, claiming that Qian had obtained permission from the court to seal up the property. The Dai family was panicked. Tang, hearing the alarm while ill, was momentarily stimulated and coughed up blood like a spring, uncontrollably, and died on the spot. Tang's wife mourned the death of her husband and, after the coffin was prepared, went to find Qian dressed in white mourning clothes and dragged him into the Public Security Bureau, shouting for justice. Qian was old and unusually frugal, accumulating assets of four to five hundred yuan. Suddenly, news spread that he had been detained by the Public Security Bureau, and there was an uproar in the city. Some who were friendly to Qian went to request bail, but were all refused. He was only allowed to be bailed out late at night, but he was already in a state of great distress.

Red Pill Manufacturing Discovered in Taizhou 89

The Huangyan Southeast Township Luqiao Town Public Security Bureau received a tip-off that Wang Guangding's house in Luxiangdian was found to be manufacturing red pills. They immediately ordered the police to go to the scene and found two small bags of red pills, totaling 1,845 pills, four bamboo sieves, one gauze sieve, a small half box of red dye, a large scale, a machine, a large bag of saccharin weighing five jins, a bag of white powder weighing twelve taels, and four white cloth bags. Wang Guangding was arrested and sent to the county government for investigation.

We have long admired this. The Second Plenary Session resolved to entrust the handling of the Guangdong situation to Mr. Yu Zuoyu, and Mr. Chen Bonan also left Guangdong for Hong Kong yesterday to return power to the Central Government. Guangdong Associations in Shanghai Jointly Telegraphed Chen Jitang to Come to His Senses and Decided to Convene a Meeting to Discuss Ways to Save the Hometown 91

Central News Agency reports: Since the changes in Guangdong and Guangxi, the entire nation has condemned them. The Guangdong Fellow Villagers Association in Shanghai and others have repeatedly telegraphed Chen, Li, and Bai, explaining the greater good. However, the speakers were earnest, but the listeners were dismissive, not only stubbornly refusing to come to their senses but also engaging in military actions, abusing the people, and undermining unification. The association has again jointly with various fellow villagers associations and organizations in Shanghai condemned their wrongdoings, urging them to follow the Central Government's orders, retreat in good time to maintain the hometown's integrity, and preserve their reputation. The original telegram is excerpted below: "Guangzhou Mr. Chen Bonan: It is recently heard that you are unwilling to accept the Plenary Session's resolutions, resisting the National Government's orders, and summoning the Guangxi army to Guangdong for defense and assistance in battle. The people of Guangdong are fleeing and avoiding the situation, which is extremely tragic. In this way, you are using the hometown as a desperate gamble, turning all of Guangdong into a battlefield, and plunging the people of Guangdong into eternal suffering. Recalling when the Guangxi army governed under Chen and Mo, the people of Guangdong still turn pale at the mention of it. As a native of Guangdong, how can you bear to inflict endless disasters on your hometown for your own personal grievances? It is also heard that you have formed a Finance Committee, ordering Guangdong and Guangxi banknotes to circulate equally, otherwise military law will be enforced. However, the exchange rate of Guangxi banknotes to Guangdong banknotes has always been 50%. If they are circulated equally, Guangxi banknotes will flood Guangdong Province, and the losses to Guangdong merchants will be incalculable. Thus, you are using war to harm Guangdong and using finance to disrupt Guangdong. Many generals in Guangdong have already obeyed the Central Government. Their righteous voice has spread, and the entire nation admires them. Why are you alone willing to be a ringleader, treating your hometown as an enemy, and causing pain to your relatives? For the sake of Guangdong and for your own sake, you should come to your senses, promptly retreat, and follow the Central Government's orders to maintain peace in Guangdong, which is to preserve your reputation. Respectfully awaiting your reply, Guangdong Fellow Villagers Association in Shanghai, Jiaying Five Counties Fellow Villagers Association, Chaozhou Fellow Villagers Association, Zhongshan Fellow Villagers Association, Dabu Fellow Villagers Association, Panyu Guild Hall, Huizhou Fellow Villagers Association, Wuhua Fellow Villagers Association, respectfully request." Moreover, as the situation has developed, the association plans to convene a general meeting of various Guangdong fellow villagers associations and influential villagers in Shanghai to discuss all ongoing matters for saving the hometown and the nation. They hope that Chen Jitang will finally come to his senses and urge the Guangxi army to immediately return to Guangxi to preserve their strength and unite against foreign aggression. The association also telegraphed Yu Hanmou to congratulate him on assuming the positions of Pacification Director and Commander-in-Chief of the Fourth Route Army, requesting him to return to his troops as soon as possible to comfort the people's longing. The original telegram is also recorded below: "Shaoguan, Sent to Commander-in-Chief Yu: Having read your telegram, we respectfully acknowledge your appointment to a high position, your dedication to public service, and your unwavering righteousness. We are immensely delighted. Our hometown has long suffered from violent politics. Recently, there has been a mobilization of troops and incitement of chaos, abusing the people. The Central Government is concerned about the difficulties and dangers and has entrusted you with a great mission, recognizing your talent and appointing you to a position of responsibility. We hope you will return to your troops as soon as possible to comfort the people's longing. All Circles Held a Memorial Service for Zhang Taiyan Yesterday, Mayor Wu, Wang Xiaolai, and Others Served as the Presidium, Cai Yuanpei Offered Flowers, and Zhou Yongneng Read the Memorial Oration 92

The memorial service for Mr. Zhang Taiyan, held by all circles in this city, took place yesterday afternoon at 4:00 PM at the Lake Society on Guizhou Road, Beijing Road. The venue was set up in the hall on the second floor. In front of the main entrance and the stage in the hall, black and white cloth arches were erected, with a horizontal banner reading "Memorial Service for Mr. Zhang Taiyan by All Circles in Shanghai." From the main entrance to the third floor, mourning couplets were hung on the walls. In the center and around the front of the venue, white silk was suspended in the air, forming flower balls. In the center of the front of the stage, hexagonal plain lanterns were hung. The portrait of the Premier was hung on the stage, with the Party and national flags on both sides. Below was the mourning hall, where the portrait of Mr. Taiyan was placed. The mourning table was adorned with several colors of fresh flowers and fruits, and a stone shield presented by the China Stone Company, inscribed with the four characters "National Mentor," was placed. The entire venue was simple, solemn, and extremely tragic.

Service Officials

Presidium: Mayor Wu, Cai Yuanpei, Yang Hu, Wang Xiaolai, Tong Xingbai, Pan Gongzhan, Du Yuesheng. Presiding Officiant: Mayor Wu. Flower Offering: Cai Yuanpei. Memorial Oration Reader: Zhou Yongneng. Master of Ceremonies: Huang Jun. Secretary General: Li Dachao. Secretaries: Zhou Guoping, Li Shizhen. Reception: Jin Tian, Cha Weihan, Chen Tongjia, Zhang Zhuo, and others.

Attending Representatives

Yesterday, representatives from various organizations and groups attended: Mayor Wu Tiecheng (represented by Pan Gongzhan), Pan Gongzhan, Cai Yuanpei, Tong Xingbai, Yang Hu, Wang Xiaolai, Zhu Qinglan, Zai Xuchu, Xue Dubi, Du Yuesheng, Zhang Xiaolin, Cai Jingjun (represented by Gu Zhaofen), Xu Xiuzhi, Sun Jingya, Liu Zhanen, Xu Jilun, Chen Aishi, Huang Renzhi, Liu Zhongying, Guo Shun, Zhang Fayao, Shen Tianxin, Qian Xinzhai, Li Dachao, Wu Yunqi, Zhu Shaoping, Zhang Zhiben, Zhang Zhenyuan, Xie Zongguan, Mao Yun, Jin Guobao, Xiang Longxun, Ge Futian, and over five hundred others.

Memorial Ceremony

At 4:30 PM, the memorial ceremony began: (1) The presidium took their seats; (2) Everyone stood at attention; (3) Music was played; (4) The most respectful salute was paid to the Party and national flags and the Premier's portrait; (5) "Love Song" was played; (6) Flowers were offered; (7) A moment of silence was observed; (8) The memorial oration was read; (9) The chairman gave a report; (10) Speeches were given; (11) The family expressed their gratitude; (12) A dirge was played; (13) The ceremony was completed.

Mr. Cai's Report

First, Chairman Cai Yuanpei gave a report, stating: "I don't know much about Mr. Zhang's childhood. One year, I went from Hangzhou to Lin'an and passed by Yuhang, where I first met Mr. Zhang. He was in his twenties and was writing the 'Qiushu'. In 1901, Zhang cut off his queue and wandered through the market, advocating for the overthrow of the Qing Dynasty. His neighbors looked at him askance. Zhang Taiyan's name was taken in admiration of Huang Tai Chong and Gu Yanwu, scholars of the late Ming and early Qing dynasties. At that time, there was a Jing Shi Bao in Hangzhou, and Zhang often wrote articles scolding the government and advocating revolution. Due to the environment, he soon came to Shanghai and wrote for the 'Subao' and 'Minbao'. When the 'Subao' case occurred, Zhang and others were arrested. Others were rescued and released, but Zhang was sentenced to three years in the Western Prison for the words 'clown' in his 'Refutation of Kang Youwei's Book'. He was in the same prison as Chen Tuian. I visited him at that time and sent him books and pocket money. When he was released from prison, Zhang shaved his head. People said they were afraid the wind would hurt his brain. Zhang laughed and said, 'I'm not afraid of knives, let alone the wind.' Then he went to Japan and lectured in Tokyo. The listeners were all older than Zhang and had deep roots in Chinese studies. For a time, he had a great influence on the students in Tokyo. Later, many professors in the Chinese literature departments of Peking University and the current National Central University were his students at that time. After middle age, he still did not forget his passion for politics and often telegraphed his views on the current situation. In recent years, he devoted himself to lecturing, but unfortunately, he did not complete his work and suddenly passed away, which makes people miss him very much."

Mr. Pan's Tribute

Next, Pan Gongzhan, representing Mayor Wu, delivered a speech, stating: "(1) We should not be ashamed of Mr. Zhang's spirit of advocating revolution in the late Qing Dynasty when we mourn him. (2) The Chinese people have always used the names of great masters to praise themselves. In fact, great masters should be recognized by the public. Mr. Zhang can be called a master of a generation. I deeply hope that his students can carry forward his great learning and his spirit. (3) Revolutionary thought and action should complement each other. Mr. Zhang pioneered the modern intellectual world and combined it with revolutionary action. He should be a model for us."

Mr. Wang's Speech

Next, Professor Wang Zai Dong of National Central University (one of Mr. Zhang's disciples) gave a speech, stating: "Mr. Taiyan often compared himself to three people: (1) Gu Tinglin, but I feel that he was even more so. It was easier for Gu, a scholar of the late Ming Dynasty, to pledge to be unyielding. Zhang was born more than 200 years after the Qing Dynasty established the country, but he was still able to maintain his unyielding spirit, which is the best example of our nation's strong resistance to foreign aggression. (2) Liu Qingtian (Ji) assisted the Ming master in his great cause and restored China. Mr. Zhang can be worthy of him. There are two people who cannot be denied credit for establishing the Republic of China: one is Mr. Sun Yat-sen, and the other is Mr. Zhang. Mr. Zhang was the main advocate of the rise of national thought in the late Qing Dynasty. (3) Wang Chong. Mr. Zhang's 'Qiushu', innovative and skeptical spirit is unattainable. However, his later thoughts have changed slightly. He said he suppressed Confucius and Yan Hui, but in fact, he started to overthrow Kang and Liang's fallacies. Mr. Zhang did not eat Qing millet, but he was an official twice in the Republic of China: once as the Commissioner for Border Affairs of the Three Northeastern Provinces in the era of Yuan Shikai, but he left after less than two months; and once as the Secretary-General of the Presidential Palace. Mr. Zhang had his far-sighted vision in the early years of the Republic of China, considering the border affairs of the Three Northeastern Provinces to be the top priority of our country's national defense. In his later years, he lectured in Suzhou and personally drafted the regulations. It was scheduled for two years, but he died in one year, which is very sad."

Family's Gratitude

Finally, Zhang's son, Dao, and son-in-law, Zhu Duomin, took the stage, representing the family, and bowed three times to thank the guests. They bowed to the presiding committee before the music played and the ceremony was completed.

Memorial Oration

On the eighteenth day of July in the twenty-fifth year of the Republic of China, Wu Tiecheng, the mayor of Shanghai, and representatives of Party, government, military, police, and various organizations, respectfully offer incense, flowers, wine, and tributes to the spirit of Mr. Da Yan, saying: He was a teacher of human ethics and a model of writing. He came out early in the revolution and spent his later years studying the classics. He did not die in prison and wrote with divine power. His words spread like the wind, promoting our Three Principles of the People. When the country was first founded, he and his wife lived in harmony. When the great thief stole the country, the republic almost collapsed. He was imprisoned again in Youli and restored the Han capital. He was a prominent figure in the National Protection War. At forty, he planned for the border; at fifty, he joined the army; at sixty-seven, he grew old in the classics. Like the unicorn appearing out of season, he grieved for the chaos of the world. His father's books are in the box, and his talented children are tending the courtyard. His outstanding students are as bright as a row of stars. The torch is passed on to ten thousand readers, forever as a reminder. His life's learning is written in his works, shining on our Party and influencing our neighbors. The East and West mourn this sage together. The national crisis is urgent, and the central government is shocked. The first order is issued, and the heroes are gathered. The annals of history are full of sorrow and glory. On the Chun Shen River, mourners are like clouds. Dare we tell the people that the truth lies in his writing. If there is nothing to express, how can the ceremony unite the people? Accept our offerings!

Eulogies

Like the Buddha, appearing in the form of all beings, this man will always be a teacher for all generations. (Wu Tiecheng) The old things are shining again, and his ambition can truly inherit Huang and Gu. The subtle tradition has not fallen, and the source is naturally connected to Yu and Sun. (Kong Xiangxi) As a pioneer of the revolution and a master of national studies, recalling the imprisonment in Lei Ting, the world was shocked to hear of the literary inquisition. Avoiding the prosperity of the sea, he became a recluse in Wu. Grieving on this day when he traveled to Penglai Island, we know that he was a terrestrial immortal. (Pan Gongzhan) Mount Tai does not move, and what it passes through transforms. Escaping the world without resentment, his death is a cause for sorrow. (Yang Hu) He is a master of simple learning, gathering the achievements since the Qianlong and Jiaqing eras, with his own system. He is a revolutionary predecessor, standing alone outside the Zhao and Song dynasties. (Hu Puan) A contemporary teacher and friend, is the unicorn's appearance only a pity for our Party? His great name is recorded in the rivers and seas, and the sinking star is a lament for all sages. (Municipal Government)

Deng Qingyang and Others Returned South Yesterday Afternoon 93

The five Central Committee members sent north by the Southwest to attend the Second Plenary Session, except for Huang Linshu, who had already returned south on the 14th, and Li Qian, who remained in Shanghai temporarily due to unfinished public and private matters, Deng Qingyang, Li Renren, Cui Guangxiu, and others left Shanghai on the Lincoln President of the Great Lai Company at 12:45 yesterday afternoon to return south. Deng and others boarded the ship from the Xinguang Wharf across the Huangpu River at 11:44. Few people knew about their departure, so only related personnel such as Huang Huapei went to the ship to see them off. Before his departure, Deng met with representatives of the Xinsheng News Agency at the New Asia Hotel. According to reports, he said, "We have been away from Guangdong for many days, and we don't know the actual extent of the current situation in Guangdong. We don't know the truth of what is reported in the newspapers and official telegrams. Since the death of Chairman Hu, Mr. Xiao Focheng has been the most senior among the comrades in the Southwest in the history of the Party and the country. Now that Mr. Xiao has left Guangdong for Hong Kong, it is conceivable that the Guangdong situation has collapsed. We still prioritize peace as the first and foremost goal. Since the Second Plenary Session formulated a plan, although the situation is still tense, we hope to find a way out of the plan and peacefully resolve everything to avoid local devastation and damage to construction. We read in the newspaper that Chen Jitang arrived in Hong Kong last night, but we are not sure if it is true because we have not received a telegram from the South. If it is true, then the war can be avoided and the Guangdong situation can be resolved. We will go to Hong Kong first to consult with Mr. Xiao about everything, and then return to Guangdong. After Guangdong is in danger, it is necessary for someone to take care of it. We are natives of Guangdong and cannot sit idly by and cannot abandon our responsibility."

Kong Xiangrong Talks About This Year's Yellow River Disaster Will Not Occur 94

Kong Xiangrong, deputy chairman of the Yellow River Conservancy Commission, arrived in Shanghai yesterday morning from Beijing to pay his respects to Finance Minister Kong and report to him. According to Kong, speaking to the Central News Agency reporter, although the Yellow River's water level is currently high, the prevention is very strict, and this year's Yellow River disaster is expected not to occur.

Eurasia's Newest and Largest Rented Aircraft Arrived in Shanghai This Morning; Two More Giant Aircraft Will Also Fly In Soon 95

Eurasia Aviation Company leased two Ju52 three-engine giant aircraft from German Lufthansa Aviation Company. They departed from Berlin on the 7th one after another to be flown to China. The first aircraft, with the emblem Dayni, made a stop in Athens for a few days due to the illness of a mechanic while flying over Greece and then continued flying east. It arrived in Yangon on the 17th and continued flying to Hong Kong yesterday morning. It is expected to arrive in Shanghai this morning. Its pilot is Luther, and there are two other co-pilots, Leidieg and radio operator Jende. The company is prepared to welcome them and has sent invitations to all sectors to participate. The second aircraft is also expected to arrive in Shanghai soon.

Various Banks Held a Meeting Yesterday, Recognizing the Capital of the Farmers' Bank 96

The Ministry of Industry established the Farmers' Bank to utilize urban capital to regulate the rural economy. Twenty-nine banks in this city have participated. The Ministry has assigned personnel to be responsible for preparations and aims to establish it at the beginning of next month. Yesterday afternoon at 4:00 PM, the banks held another meeting at the Bank Club to discuss and determine the methods of underwriting fixed capital and decided to hold a follow-up meeting next week to elect directors. The details are as follows:

Participating Banks

The organizational outline of the Farmers' Bank was revised and passed after Industry Minister Wu Dingchang convened two meetings with banking circles in Shanghai and then began preparations. The bank will be located in Nanjing and is scheduled to be established at the beginning of next month. Twenty-eight banks in this city, including China and Communications, originally participated. Now Jiangsu Bank has joined, totaling 29 banks. These banks have always attached great importance to agricultural loan business. In addition to independently handling it in various places with remarkable results, 19 banks, including China and Communications, have jointly formed the China Agricultural Cooperative Loan Syndicate to specialize in investing in special products such as Shaanxi cotton, Anhui rice, and Guangdong sugar, which is of great benefit to farmers. The Farmers' Bank focuses on regulating general agricultural products and circulating the rural economy, complementing various banks and cooperative syndicates, benefiting farmers more widely and deeply, so the banks all expressed their agreement.

Attending Representatives

The following bank representatives attended yesterday's meeting of participating banks: Guo Wenhe of Agricultural and Commercial, Zhu Runsheng of China Farmers, Sun Ruihuang of Xinhua, Lu Zidong of Jiangsu, Wu Rencang of Jiangsu Farmers, Ye Zhuotang of Central Savings Association, Hu Bijiang of Communications, Wang Shaoxian of Salt, Wu Muhan of Donglai, Zou Bingwen of Shanghai, Zhang Xinyi of China, Song Hanzhang, Bei Songsun, Zhang Zhuyu of China National Products, Qi Yunqing of China Agricultural and Industrial, Wu Xizhi of Postal Savings and Remittance Bureau, Xu Xinliu of Zhejiang Industry, Zhou Desun of the Four Banks, Qian Xinzhi, Zhou Jiyun of Zhongnan, Sun Jingxi of Zhongfu, Chen Duoru of Zhejiang Industrial, Wang Boyuan of China Reclamation, Wu Yunzhai of Jincheng, Ye Fuxiao of Dalu, Yao Yinpeng of Zhonghui, Pan Yifen of Zhongyi Trust, Yuan Mengqin of Quangong, Hu Xian of Siming, Zhou Wusan of Tongshang, Shen Guangyan of China Industrial, and Rao Taoshu of Guohua. Secretary Gu Chengan of the Bankers' Association also attended and took notes.

Chairman's Report

After the meeting opened, Qian Xinzhi was publicly elected as chairman and reported that the Farmers' Bank had a total fund of 30 million yuan, which was stipulated to be subscribed by participating banks within five years. He asked for discussion on how to underwrite the 5 million yuan this year. After public resolution, one-fifth, which is 1 million yuan, will be determined by various agricultural banks, such as China Agricultural and Industrial, China Farmers, and Jiangsu Farmers. The remaining 4 million yuan will be borne by the banks according to the proportion of the total amount of savings deposits, estimated to be 1% of the total amount of savings, which is 500 million yuan. The detailed figures will be determined after calculation. As for the election of 12 directors that the bank should elect, it was decided to convene a meeting next week to determine the selection.

Establish Training Class

The Ministry of Industry has established an agricultural economic and technical personnel training class to train specialized personnel to serve in various places as the Farmers' Bank is about to open. The training class is divided into advanced and elementary classes, each taught for four months and interned for two months. After graduation, the best performers will be given priority for employment. The monthly salary for the advanced class starts at 80 yuan, and the monthly salary for the elementary class starts at 40 yuan. The recruitment matters are entrusted to the Agricultural College of Jinling University in Nanjing and the Law School of Peking University. Registration starts today and ends on the 31st of this month. The examination dates are August 8th and 9th. The quota for each class is 40 people.

The joint meeting of chambers of commerce of fifteen provinces and cities convened by the Shanghai Chamber of Commerce. In addition to the fifteen representatives from the Hankou, Taiyuan, Shandong, and Zhenjiang Chambers of Commerce who have already registered, Luo Huizong of the Hubei Provincial Chamber of Commerce Federation, Yu Xiaochuan, Qian Sunqing, and Wang Jingting of the Jiangsu Provincial Chamber of Commerce Federation, Zhou Zishi of the Jiangxi Provincial Chamber of Commerce Federation, Chen Xinyan of the Nanjing Chamber of Commerce, Tao Yutang and Yun Gu of the Wuhu Chamber of Commerce, and Liu Wenting and Wang Deting of the Qingdao Chamber of Commerce have registered, totaling representatives from eight provinces and three cities.

Guangdong Exchange Rate Soars Yesterday 99

Trade between Shanghai and Guangdong has been stagnant for some time. Since the report on the 18th that the Guangdong situation could be stabilized, the amount of remittances from this city to Guangzhou has increased sharply. It is reported that in order to facilitate remittances for Guangdong merchants, the Kwok Wah Bank has specially established a Guangdong Remittance Department in its Hongkou branch, with particularly low exchange rates, which is very convenient for Guangdong merchants. Yesterday's market price was 617 yuan of Shanghai legal tender for 1,000 yuan of Guangdong legal tender, with as much exchange as possible, and approximately over 200,000 yuan was remitted.

Merrell Called on Minister Kung Yesterday to Discuss Smuggling Prevention Measures on the Beining Railway 100

According to the Shin Shih News Agency, Japanese ronin are engaged in large-scale smuggling in North China. In addition to sending a letter to the Beining Railway Bureau, requesting them to follow the previous order issued by the Executive Yuan and instructing the railway police to protect the customs officers stationed at the stations to facilitate inspection, the Tianjin Customs also requested Chief Inspector of Customs Merrell to quickly determine appropriate measures. Mr. Merrell went to the Central Bank yesterday to meet with Minister of Finance Kung Hsiang-hsi to report on tax matters and discuss measures to prevent smuggling on the Beining Railway. It is now reported that a general decision has been made to first send Ansell, the Director of the Anti-Smuggling General Inspection Department of the Ministry of Finance, to the north to negotiate smuggling prevention with the Beining Railway Bureau and set up anti-smuggling inspection sub-offices along the line. In response to the request from Tianjin Customs, several officers will be dispatched to Tianjin to assist with customs anti-smuggling duties. As for the anti-smuggling affairs on the southern sections of the Jinpu and Pinghan Railways, since the establishment of inspection offices along the line to take responsibility for strict inspection, considerable results have been achieved. In order to intercept the southward transportation of smuggled goods from eastern Hebei, the Inspectorate General of Customs will pay close attention to anti-smuggling duties along the Beining Railway. Once Ansell, the Director of the Anti-Smuggling General Inspection Department of the Ministry of Finance, goes north, a method can be negotiated and implemented.

Shao Lizi Arrives in Shanghai to Discuss Suppression of Bandits and Construction in the Northwest; Post-Banditry Rehabilitation Requires Funds; Rural Areas Gradually Prospering; Construction Expenditures are Significant; Opium Planting to be Completely Banned Next Year 101

Shao Lizi, Chairman of the Shaanxi Provincial Government, and his wife left Nanjing on the night express train on the 17th and arrived at the North Station in Shanghai at around 7:00 AM on the 18th. They immediately went to their residence to rest. Zhang Gongquan, Minister of Railways, also arrived in Shanghai on the same train as Mr. Shao. Mr. Shao plans to stay in Shanghai for a few days before going to Nanjing and then returning to Shaanxi to preside over provincial affairs. According to Mr. Shao, the military campaign to suppress bandits in the Northwest is progressing smoothly, and bandit areas have been successively recovered. However, the rehabilitation problem is quite difficult due to economic constraints. Construction in the Northwest, such as roads and water conservancy, is also proceeding according to plan. The annual cotton harvest in the Northwest has improved significantly, so the rural economy is gradually prospering, and people's lives are recovering. This year's wheat harvest was only 30% due to unfavorable weather, with warm winters and cold springs. However, the people are not panicked because the current weather is suitable, and if there are no changes, this year's cotton harvest could be double that of last year. Shaanxi's finances for the 24th year can be balanced, with no new deficits. Furthermore, within the expenditures for the 24th year, there are over two million for road construction and six to seven hundred thousand yuan for water conservancy construction. However, it will be difficult to balance revenues and expenditures for the 25th year because the recovery of the bandit areas in northern Shaanxi requires funds for relief and construction everywhere, and the expenses for the militia are considerable. In addition, Shaanxi's opium ban is proceeding according to plan. As of recently, only 19 counties still have opium cultivation, and this will soon be reduced. Therefore, opium tax revenue has decreased sharply, making it difficult to balance revenues and expenditures. Shaanxi must completely ban opium planting in the second half of next year, and the finances for the 26th year are expected to be even more difficult. Currently, they are planning ways to remedy the situation.

French Concession Taxpayers' Association Establishes Real Estate Research Association 102

The Chinese Taxpayers' Association of the French Concession recently established a Real Estate Research Committee, appointing Mao Yun, Huang Xianggu, Gong Jingyan, and Qu Zhenhua as members. The first article of its regulations states that the committee is organized in accordance with Article 9 of the organizational rules of the Executive Committee of the Chinese Taxpayers' Association of the French Concession and is named the Real Estate Research Committee of the Chinese Taxpayers' Association of the French Concession. The second article states that the purpose of the committee is to study real estate issues within the concession and promote public interests. The third article states that the committee shall have nine members, who shall be mutually elected from among the executive and supervisory committee members of the Chinese Taxpayers' Association of the French Concession, with a term of one year. The fourth article states that the committee shall handle the following matters: matters relating to real estate registration; matters relating to real estate research. The fifth article states that the committee may hire experts as consultants to promote the progress of committee affairs. The sixth article states that the committee shall hold one meeting per month, with the chairman temporarily appointed by the committee members. Additional meetings may be held when necessary. The seventh article states that the Chinese and foreign committee members and consultants may be invited to attend the meeting when the committee meets. The eighth article states that these regulations shall be implemented upon approval by the Executive Committee of the Chinese Taxpayers' Association of the French Concession.

Postal Remittances Bureau to Launch Children's Savings Program; Pilot Program to Begin with Enrolled Children; Program to Begin in the Fall Semester 103

The Postal Savings and Remittances Bureau of the Ministry of Communications has formulated savings regulations and implementation measures for the children's savings program and is currently expediting procedures, planning to begin implementation in the fall semester. The details are as follows:

Pilot Program to Begin in the Fall: The Postal Savings and Remittances Bureau's plan to implement children's savings originated at the beginning of this year. As this year is Children's Year, the Ministry of Communications instructed the bureau to plan and implement the program to cultivate the virtue of saving in children. The bureau's savings department then drafted detailed savings regulations and implementation measures, which were submitted to the Ministry of Communications for approval in mid-June. A pilot program will begin with enrolled children. The ministry requested the Executive Yuan to instruct the Ministry of Education to direct educational institutions in each province and city to assist in the implementation. After receiving the order, the bureau also distributed notices to savings bureaus in various locations. It is reported that, with the exception of provinces such as Guizhou and Guangxi that do not have savings programs, other locations will simultaneously launch the program in the fall.

Savings Methods: The children's savings method is the same as ordinary passbook savings. School children under the age of 20 may register to save. A savings passbook can be opened with as little as half a yuan. The bureau will print savings stamps in denominations of five fen and one jiao. When registering to save, a savings grid or savings bag will be provided to paste the stamps or store the money. Savings can be deposited only after one yuan is accumulated. However, savings deposits per household may not exceed 20 yuan per month, and the total amount may not exceed 200 yuan. Savings withdrawals may not exceed two times per month, and each withdrawal may not exceed one-fifth of the savings.

The interest rate is half a li higher than ordinary savings, calculated at a weekly rate of five li.

Promotion and Implementation: In order to effectively promote the program, the bureau will be assisted by schools in various locations. In addition to printing various promotional materials and savings brochures for schools to promote, the bureau will also entrust schools to sell savings stamps and regularly send staff to schools to collect savings and open savings accounts. For encouragement, the bureau will create a savings promotion trophy. The three individuals who introduce the most children's savings accounts will be awarded a savings promotion trophy as a souvenir. The bureau has also created a savings mailbox for children to purchase and store savings. It is reported that the launch date is approximately in mid-October, right after schools start. Currently, procedures are being expedited.

China National Aviation Corporation's Hankou-Xunyang Route Suspended; Temporary Nanjing-Xunyang Route to be Operated Instead 108

Shanghai Aviation News Agency: Since the China National Aviation Corporation's Shanghai-Chengdu route began using large land-based aircraft, the Jiujiang Airport has been unsuitable for the take-off and landing of large aircraft, resulting in the suspension of the station for a long time. The runway reconstruction has not yet been completed. To facilitate passengers and mail, a temporary Hankou-Xunyang flight was launched on the 15th of this month to make up for the gap. Now it is felt that passengers and mail going up and down the line must go through Hankou when transferring to the large aircraft on the Shanghai-Chengdu line, which is inconvenient. Therefore, it has been decided to suspend the Hankou-Xunyang route from the 2nd of this month and operate a temporary Nanjing-Xunyang flight on the same day, still using the Jinan seaplane. It will depart from Nanjing at 9:00 AM every day (connecting with the westbound aircraft arriving in Nanjing at 10:20 AM from Shanghai at 7:00 AM).

It will arrive in Xunyang at 11:20 AM and depart from Xunyang at 12:00 PM, arriving in Nanjing at 2:20 PM (connecting with the eastbound aircraft departing from Shanghai). For ticket and freight prices and all details, please call 90529 to inquire with the Aviation Transportation Company.

Red Swastika Society Reports on Disaster Relief in Huoqiu 110

Huoqiu County in Anhui Province has suffered from disasters for many years. The drought last year was particularly severe. The spring famine this year has left the population with nothing to eat. Tree bark and grass roots have been completely consumed. The Red Swastika Society specially raised relief funds and publicly appointed Liu Xichun, the president of the Wuhu Red Swastika Society, along with relief commissioners Chen Tianru, Zhou Jingbingquan, Shao Yupuo, and Tang Yuanding, to bring the funds to the county to implement relief efforts. They have now completed their work. It is now reported that the Shanghai General Office of the Society has received reports from the Huoqiu Red Swastika Society and various legal organizations in the county regarding the work of Mr. Liu and others in the county, which are very detailed. Excerpts of the report are as follows: This county's relief work has been completed after Mr. Liu arrived in the county and worked for several months. The report on the various tasks is as follows:

Inspection and Relief Procedures: The Swastika Society notified the Bao chiefs to create a register and send it to the Society for review. After the review, the relief workers, together with the Bao chiefs, investigated each household, personally issuing relief tickets to the victims. Every day, they advanced in order according to the route. Even in remote areas and villages where bandits frequented, they personally went to interview and issue relief tickets.

Relief Ticket Levels: Divided into three levels: one yuan, two yuan, and three yuan. Ordinary poor people are all considered ordinary people. Those who are widowed, orphaned, lonely, elderly, weak, disabled, or poor are all issued heavy tickets.

Distribution of Relief Funds: The county government dispatched personnel to go to the central locations of each disaster area, along with supervisors, to jointly distribute funds. Every day, the relief tickets exchanged for funds were collected and stamped with a "Jointly Distributed" seal. The supervisors calculated and registered them daily. In addition, Mr. Liu established a porridge kitchen in the disaster area and personally supervised the distribution, showing extreme diligence.

Six Robbers Sentenced for Murdering Housewife Last Year; Case of Zhou Jinlan's Home Being Robbed 111

At 11:30 PM on April 7th last year, robbers broke into the home of local Zhou Jinlan at No. 3 Northeast Lujiayan in Yangsi District, Pudong, and robbed the house. They tied up the family members and plundered the house, stealing over 100 yuan in cash, as well as gold jewelry and clothing. Because Zhou's wife, Zhou Xi, became anxious and grabbed the robbers, she was strangled and beaten with iron rods, resulting in immediate death. Afterwards, Zhou's son, Zhou Jinfang, discovered that his mother had been killed by robbers and reported the incident to the local court, which sent personnel to verify the facts and ordered the arrest of the murderers. Subsequently, patrol officer Xiao Jing of the Yangsiqiao Police Station and detective Li Guisheng and Huang Liansheng of the Tangqiao Police Station successively arrested the main offenders Zhou Caigen, Tang Lingen, Zhou Agen, and Xia Wansheng, as well as accomplices Zhu Lingen and Zhou Asong, and suspects Ren Kuanfu and Zhang Xiangsheng, totaling eight people, and sent them to the local court. Prosecutor Bu Benxulin filed a public prosecution. After repeated investigations and debates by Presiding Judge Cai Dingcheng, the verdict was announced yesterday. Zhou Caigen, Tang Lingen, Zhou Agen, and Xia Wansheng were each sentenced to life imprisonment. Zhu Lingen was sentenced to five years of imprisonment. Zhou Asong was sentenced to two years and six months of imprisonment. Ren Kuanfu and Zhang Xiangsheng were found not guilty. After the verdict was announced, the guilty defendants were returned to custody, and the innocent defendants were each released on bail with a deposit of 3,000 yuan and guarantees from three reputable stores, pending the expiration of the appeal period before the sentences are executed separately.

Unmarried Couple's Affair; Issue of an Affair; Sister-in-Law and Adultery; Beating in the Outhouse 112

Guan Yao, an elderly woman from Yuyao, 67 years old, lived at No. 2 Songqing Lane, Xiexu Branch Road, at the home of her eldest grandson-in-law, Zhu Jinkun. The woman had a younger granddaughter, Guan Xiaofa, 16 years old, who was betrothed by the woman to Chen Shusheng, a 34-year-old Qingjiang native living next door at No. 4, as his fiancée last year. They have not yet married. However, Chen Shusheng could not wait and lured Guan Xiaofa out, continuously meeting in hotels for pleasure, which was discovered by Zhu Jinkun. So, while Chen was defecating in the outhouse, he gathered a crowd to beat him up, causing an incident. The police arrested them and sent them to the local court, charging Chen Shusheng with disrupting public morals and raping a girl under the age of sixteen, and charging Zhu Jinkun with assault, filing separate lawsuits. Yesterday, the criminal court heard the case. Official asked Zhu Jinkun, who testified that he was 25 years old, from Nantong, and that Guan Xiaofa was his wife's younger sister, and Guan Yao was his grandmother-in-law, and that he did not beat Chen Shusheng, etc. At this point, Official asked Chen Shusheng, who testified that last year he had been with Guan Xiaofa in a room at the Far East Hotel once, at the Dafang Hotel twice, and at Changhan once. Each time, she (referring to Xiaofa) asked me to go with her, buy things, and then go to the Grand Stage to see a play. Because it was late, we went to rent a room together. After this started, we often went out, etc. Official asked, Did you know how old she was? He replied, Eighteen years old. It was written on the wedding certificate at the time. Now the wedding certificate has been taken away by them. At this point, Official asked Guan Xiaofa, who testified that she was sixteen years old, a minor, born on May 17th, and that she first had sexual intercourse with Chen Shusheng in December last year, about five or six times in total, etc. Guan Yao testified that she was 67 years old, and Guan Xiaofa was her granddaughter. Her parents are both dead, and I raised her. After I issued a wedding certificate to betroth my granddaughter to Chen Shusheng last year, I learned that they were having an affair. Please investigate, etc. At this point, the Official asked Chen Shusheng again, When were you beaten by them? He replied, On the 18th of last month, I went to the outhouse to defecate, and Zhu Jinkun called ten people to beat me. They wanted to extort money from me. Official asked, Is it because you were having an affair with Guan Xiaofa that they beat you? He replied, I have no idea. At this point, Zhu testified that he was already asleep at the time and was called by his grandmother-in-law, who said that Xiaofa had been forcibly taken away by Chen, so he went to look for her. I didn't hit him. Official asked, Who hit him then? He replied, I don't know. The Official immediately announced the end of the debate and scheduled the verdict for the 21st.

Qingliang Temple Monk Again Files Suit Regarding Property Dispute: Claims 28 Rooms Were Self-Built, Case Adjourned to the 23rd for Re-examination of Documents 113

Qingliang Chan Temple on Xin Zha Road, one of the four major temple properties in Shanghai, was established through years of tireless effort by its abbot, Qinghai Monk, who solicited donations from all sides. Its architecture is grand, and its incense offerings are flourishing. However, the temple's land belonged to Sheng Xuanhuai, a former Qing dynasty palace guardian, and was later divided among his descendants, Sheng Yuyou, who managed the property. Qinghai Monk leased the land from Sheng Yuyou. However, in the 17th year of the Republic (1928), the Sheng family abruptly mortgaged the land to the British firm Jardine Matheson & Co. for 350,000 silver dollars, transferring all property rights. Jardine Matheson, relying on the five-year lease agreement with Qingliang Temple, notified the temple to vacate upon its expiration. Qinghai Monk refused, arguing that the temple was built through years of tireless fundraising. Jardine Matheson then filed a lawsuit in the Civil Division of the First Special Court. After the case arose, philanthropists such as Wang Yiting and Zhu Qinglan, aiming to protect Buddhism, formed a maintenance association and invited prominent figures from Shanghai to mediate. However, these efforts were unsuccessful, and the court ruled against Qinghai Monk, with the final verdict rendered. As the execution date approached, Qinghai Monk hired a lawyer to accuse the property owner, Sheng Yuyou, of perjury in the Criminal Division of the First Special Court. As previously reported, Qingliang Temple now claims that 21 of the temple's rooms were self-built, and an additional seven rooms were also self-built. Therefore, these 28 rooms are not the property of the Sheng family. They have hired lawyer Lu Qi to file a suit of objection to the enforcement with the Civil Division of the First Special Court against Jardine Matheson. Yesterday morning at nine o'clock, Judge Wang Shanxiang presided over the hearing in the Fourteenth Civil Court. Representatives from the Buddhist Association and the maintenance association were present to observe. Jardine Matheson was represented by lawyer Ding Rong, while property owner Sheng Yuyou was represented by lawyer Xu Shihao. The judge, stating that the case required reviewing previous case files for clarity, adjourned the hearing to 8:20 AM on the 23rd of this month.

Wang Baoqing, a Ningbo native in his forties and the manager of the Central Dance School on Zhejiang Road, married a young woman from Dinghai named Ms. Chuan. Rickshaw Guild Holds Meeting Yesterday: Establishes Relief Department 117

The Rickshaw Industry Guild convened a meeting of its members yesterday afternoon at four o'clock. Over twenty people attended, including Gu Shao'an, Gu Songmao, Wang Kunyi, Yin Zhiling, He Wanli, and Qin Yangzhou. The meeting was chaired by Yi Chunshan. As a result of the discussion, a rickshaw puller relief department was established. The articles of association are as follows: Article 1: This department is organized in accordance with Article 17, Chapter 5 of the Guild's constitution. Article 2: The purpose of this department is to improve the lives of rickshaw pullers, raise their status, and increase their welfare, based on the spirit of labor-management cooperation. Article 3: This department is subordinate to the Executive Committee of the Shanghai Rickshaw Industry Guild. Article 4: The business of this department is to improve the lives of rickshaw pullers, including the following items: (A) Promoting the education of rickshaw pullers and their children. (B) Providing medical treatment and medication for rickshaw pullers' illnesses. (C) Improving the housing of rickshaw pullers and planning the construction of new rickshaw puller villages. (D) Providing loans and consumer cooperation for rickshaw pullers. (E) Promoting savings among rickshaw pullers. (F) Seeking redress for rickshaw pullers who have been unjustly prosecuted. (G) Providing coffins for rickshaw pullers who have died. (H) Other matters beneficial to the actual lives of rickshaw pullers. Article 5: The main office of this department is located in the Taihe Building on Laoquan Road, with branch offices in the eastern, southern, western, and northern districts to handle various matters. Article 6: This department shall have one director and two deputy directors, to be elected by the Executive Committee. Article 7: The expenses of this department shall be borne by the rickshaw owners. Each rickshaw shall pay a monthly fee of thirty cents, including coffin costs. The methods for collecting the fees shall be determined separately. Article 8: This department shall have seven economic management committee members to manage the department's finances with seriousness. The candidates are as follows: One representative from the Municipal Chamber of Commerce, one representative from the Chinese Taxpayers Association, two prominent figures from society, and three representatives from the rickshaw owners. Article 9: This department may invite several consultants from the guild and related organizations and groups. Article 10: The working plan and detailed rules of this department shall be determined separately. Article 11: These simple rules shall be implemented after being approved by the Executive Committee and reported to the competent authorities for approval. Article 12: Matters not covered in these simple rules may be proposed to the Executive Committee for approval and reported to the competent authorities for amendment.

Xu Wenliang, a Cantonese residing at No. 1305 Yu Yuan Road, currently the Chinese manager of Mobil Oil, was kidnapped by six or seven robbers at approximately 2:00 AM on the 13th of this month, who tricked him into opening the door and took him away by car, also stealing silver dollars and diamond rings. French Concession: Dispute Over Increasing Fenyu Tax 122

The Fenyu industry in the French Concession of this city has been embroiled in a dispute over increased taxes for half a month, which remains unresolved. The Municipal Chamber of Commerce of this city sent a letter to all the Chinese directors of the French Concession, requesting their sympathy and assistance so that the dispute could be resolved as soon as possible. The original letter stated: "To whom it may concern, according to a letter from the Fenyu Industry Guild on the 15th of this month, 'Our members who operate in the French Concession number over one hundred. Recently, due to the economic downturn, business has been declining. However, since last year, the French Municipal Council has suddenly doubled the monthly tax, such as increasing the tax of one dollar and forty cents to two dollars and eighty cents. There are also increased table taxes without any standard. If merchants argue with reason, they are ignored. If they pay late, the electricity is cut off and business is prohibited. Furthermore, investigators are sent, and there are various investigation fees. At this time of economic hardship, they rely on the special power of politics to arbitrarily levy excessive taxes. Merchants have no means of appeal. Please find a way to provide assistance.' The recent regulations on classified business hygiene taxes promulgated by the council have resulted in increased taxes for various industries, but there is no clear reason or standard for these increases. If the size of the storefront is used as the standard, the tax rate often increases dramatically even if the storefront remains the same. If the prosperity of the business is used as the standard, the general economic situation is one of decline, so what is the reason for increasing taxes? The contents of the letter from your council to the French Municipal Council detail these circumstances and represent the general opinion of the merchants in the area. The Fenyu industry consists of small-scale businesses, and the impact is particularly severe. We hereby request that your directors provide sympathetic assistance and earnestly negotiate with the council to reduce the tax rate. This is our sincere hope."

Miscellaneous Grain Exchange Announces: Exemption from Margin 123

Previously, due to soaring market prices, the Miscellaneous Grain Exchange stipulated on July 3rd that a margin of 500 yuan must be paid for each unit of wheat traded and on July 9th stipulated that a margin of 400 yuan must be paid for each unit of oil and 200 yuan for each unit of cake in order to prevent speculators from manipulating the market. The Brokers Association recently sent a letter to the Exchange's Board of Directors requesting that the margin be restored to facilitate business, as the market has now stabilized. After deliberation, the Exchange's Board of Directors decided to exempt all pre-payment of margin, effective yesterday. However, payment must be made the day after the transaction. The Board of Directors issued an announcement yesterday, stating: "The resolutions of the 25th meeting of the 7th Board of Directors on July 17th, in addition to informing the Brokers Association for their information, are hereby recorded and announced. It is hoped that all brokers will be informed. Special announcement: Broker Association Letter No. 16: According to a joint letter from 23 brokers, including Chang Yi Jin Ji He, requesting the restoration of the margin for the purchase and sale of various goods, it was resolved that the pre-payment of margin for the purchase and sale of various goods will be abolished from today. However, the purchase and sale contracts must be paid and received the day after the transaction. Failure to do so will result in the suspension of new purchases and sales. Further announcements will be made when the market stabilizes. Regarding the early delivery and release of spot goods, it was resolved that, in addition to the Exchange's own machine orders, all other goods may be delivered and released in advance as per the rules. If discounting is required, interest will be calculated on a current basis at 3% above the Zhuang Bank's deposit rate, and the cargo price will be calculated at 80% of the selling price, but it must be based on the Exchange's inspection form and a written application for advance delivery and release of spot goods must be submitted. The application form will be printed and prepared by the Exchange. Regarding the storage period for sesame seeds, it was resolved that the sesame seed trading rules stipulate that trading will be suspended during the months of August, September, and October each year. The Exchange's responsibility for storage should be responsible until August 10th. The Exchange will not be responsible for any liability after the deadline. The following clause will be added to the Exchange's Rule 13: (Storage period: The Exchange's liability period is up to August 10th each year. The Exchange will not be responsible for any liability after the deadline)."

Yesterday's Continued Hearing: Tongyi Illegally Pledges Debt Certificates Case; Xu Ji and Others State They Were Unaware of the Contents; Court Orders the Defendants to Appear Next Time 132

Tongyi Trust Company declared bankruptcy on the 15th of last month due to financial difficulties and entrusted lawyer Li Zuyu and accountant Xi Yushu to handle the liquidation. The company's chairman and general manager, Huang Suchu, immediately fled, prompting general creditors to form a creditor group to protect their deposit interests and discuss countermeasures. The Jin Ye and Yang Muzhai households, whose government bonds deposited with the company had been pledged, asserted that Huang Suchu and all directors, supervisors, the deputy manager, and assistants should bear criminal responsibility for embezzlement and breach of trust. They filed a lawsuit with the First Special District Court, which has already held a preliminary hearing, as reported in this newspaper. However, the number of depositors whose government bonds were pledged by the company to other banks is considerable. Following the Jin Ye households' lawsuit, now five more households, including Lu Tangji, Huang Qiwen, Wu Zhongheng, Wu Xuepeng, and Yao Songtang, have also entrusted lawyer Zhang Yifan and others to file a criminal lawsuit for embezzlement and breach of trust with the First Special Court against Huang Suchu and other responsible parties, seeking to recover the value of their bonds. These households had entrusted the company with the safekeeping of various unified government bonds, including 20-year salt tax bonds and 22-year customs tax bonds, totaling tens of thousands of dollars, all of which were pledged. Furthermore, other creditors, including Xu Yeji, Xu Yeshi, and six other households, discovered that the company's total assets on the day of its bankruptcy were 6,319,589.34 yuan, while its total liabilities amounted to 6,350,952.37 yuan, with savings deposits constituting the largest portion, reaching over 2.8 million yuan, followed by insurance savings, ordinary deposits, etc. Since the liabilities exceeded the total assets, they petitioned for bankruptcy. Under the review of Judge Xu Fuki of the First Special Court, it was ruled yesterday to declare Tongyi Trust Company bankrupt on July 17th at 11:00 AM. It is expected that a bankruptcy administrator will be appointed soon to handle creditor and debtor registration procedures in accordance with the law. The company's debt disputes are likely to shift towards liquidation. As for the four criminal cases filed against Huang Suchu and others by Jin Ye and the other seven plaintiffs who had deposited government bonds, Judge Zhong Qing continued the joint hearing yesterday afternoon. The defendants who appeared were Xu Jiqing, Zhou Shouliang, Guo Yushang, Zhou Longzhan, and Yu Weiqin. The others, including Huang Suchu, Liu Fangyuan, Sun Xinchong, Liu Zikang, Liu Ning, Xiong Muqu, Jiang Liu, Fu Zhuyin, Wu Jingwen, and Deng Dongming, did not appear in court. The court questioned the five defendants who were present. Xu, Zhou, and Guo all admitted to serving as directors but stated that they did not hold actual positions. Therefore, they were unaware of the company's internal workings. Although the chairman presented business reports, asset and liability statements, and other documents at each board meeting, they were unable to detect the internal emptiness. Consequently, the board was initially unaware of the disposal of depositors' government bonds. The company had collected over two million yuan each in savings and ordinary deposits, which are currently being expedited for liquidation. The minutes of the board meetings were kept by the managing director, Liu Fangyuan, and Huang Suchu. The lawyers for Xu Jiqing and Zhou Shouliang, Xu Shihao, added some explanation. Zhou Longzhan and Jin Weiqin both stated that they were not directors and had no knowledge of the disposal of government bonds. Huang Suchu's lawyer, Wang Xiaowen, stated that Huang had left Shanghai quietly after the company's failure and that his family was also unaware of his current location. Subsequently, the lawyers for the other absent defendants also stated the reasons for their absence. However, the plaintiffs' lawyers requested that arrest warrants be issued for the absent defendants. Judge Zhong instructed the defendants' lawyers to inform their clients to appear in court, stating that regardless of whether they should bear responsibility, they must submit to trial and that evasion would not solve the problem. He then ordered a recess and scheduled another hearing.

Regulations for the French Concession: Eliminating Mosquitoes and Handling Garbage 133

The French Concession Public Works Bureau has issued regulations to promote public health within the concession, specifically regarding the elimination of mosquitoes and the handling of garbage. The details are as follows:

Mosquito Elimination Measures

The Public Works Bureau has announced mosquito elimination measures. (1) Adult mosquitoes mostly stay close to where they hatched, so very few fly in from far away. (2) Mosquito larvae must come to the surface to breathe air. Spreading kerosene on the surface of the water can cut off the air supply and cause them to suffocate and die. (3) Kerosene should be applied to all water that cannot be drained. If water needs to be drawn, it should be taken from the bottom so that the water quality is not affected and there is no oily taste. (4) When spreading kerosene on the water surface, it must cover the entire surface. For small areas of water, the oil can be poured directly on the surface, or a hand-held sprayer can be used to apply it. For large areas of water, a sprayer should be used to cover the entire surface. (5) Empty cans, water jars, and flower vases that collect water should be emptied once a week. Even water troughs for chickens and dogs should be washed and refilled once a week. (6) All useless small ponds, empty pools, and low-lying areas that can collect rainwater must be filled in or drained. (7) All wells, cisterns, water tanks, and various water storage containers must be fitted with tin lids to prevent mosquitoes from laying eggs in them. (8) Any areas of standing water where kerosene cannot be applied should be stocked with small fish (such as goldfish and spiny fish) that can eat the larvae. (9) Keep an eye out for standing or leaking water in drainage ditches and downspouts. Even covered wells and tanks should be inspected regularly for leaks or damage. All water leaks, ditches, pools, and other places should be checked frequently. While applying kerosene, be sure to search along the way for various water channels and puddles to ensure they are cleaned. (10) Kerosene should be poured wherever mosquitoes lay their eggs or where they can lay their eggs. All kinds of aquatic plants, weeds near wells and ponds, and water holes that can provide shelter for mosquitoes should be regularly cleared. In vacant lots or courtyards, bricks, tiles, bottles, and cans that can collect rainwater should also be diligently removed. (11) In areas where many mosquitoes congregate, mosquito coils can be burned to eliminate them. Dead mosquitoes should be collected and burned. (12) All residents of the concession should actively work to eliminate mosquitoes, starting with their own homes and then helping neighbors to clear mosquito breeding grounds. The success of this summer's mosquito eradication efforts depends entirely on the enthusiasm and mutual assistance of residents within the concession. The Health Department of this Bureau always has kerosene available for public needs. Anyone can come and claim it. (For any questions regarding the above mosquito eradication work, please contact the Health Bureau at No. 840 Xujiahui Road.)

Garbage Disposal Regulations

Each household in the French Concession should provide itself with a light, covered garbage can in its main or secondary building for the purpose of dumping the day's household garbage. The Bureau has a model garbage can for sale, which all households can purchase. Unless otherwise agreed upon by the Bureau and the property owner, all garbage collectors employed by the Bureau are not allowed to enter private residences, private roads, or alleys. Each household should move its garbage can to the roadside in the early morning when the garbage truck passes by. The garbage inside the garbage can should be emptied by the Bureau's collectors. It is not allowed to dump garbage on public roads, vacant land, or in rivers. Do not move the garbage can to the roadside before the garbage truck has passed. Do not leave the garbage can on the roadside after the garbage truck has passed. The Bureau may, at the request of the landlord, clean up the garbage in private roads and alleys, but the landlord must pay a handling fee in advance every six months. The amount of this fee should be equal to 4% of the total monthly rent of all the houses in that location. The garbage truck's operating hours are as follows: From April 1st to September 30th each year, from 5:00 AM to 8:00 AM; From October 1st to March 31st of the following year, from 6:00 AM to 9:00 AM. Each garbage truck has a bell that rings as it passes to alert residents. Anyone who violates these regulations will be fined from one to five yuan. Repeat offenders may be fined double. (Note) The term "garbage" refers to the kitchen waste and dust collected from the home. Leaves from the garden, animal feces, or bricks and soil should not be considered garbage and should be removed by the residents themselves. The Bureau would like to remind all residents of the French Concession to be aware of the many harms of dumping garbage on the road (such as breeding flies and toxic bacteria). It is hoped that all residents of the concession will abide by the regulations in good faith.

The Social Affairs Bureau Again Modifies Flour Price Limits 134

The Social Affairs Bureau had previously imposed limits on the price of flour due to the soaring market price, believing that speculators were manipulating it. The limits were set at 3.05 yuan for goods delivered in July, August, and September, 3.08 yuan for October, 3.11 yuan for November, and 3.14 yuan for December, and prices were not allowed to exceed these limits. However, due to active sales to other areas, prices soared, so the bureau submitted a request for a grace period, which was approved. The bureau announced yesterday: "We have now received instruction No. 6767 from the Shanghai Municipal Social Affairs Bureau, approving the temporary granting of grace periods for the monthly trading limits on goods in the market, with new regulations to be followed. We must all comply. Any transactions exceeding these price limits will not be recorded in the market accounts. In addition to posting these instructions, this announcement is made." At the same time, another announcement stated: "Starting today, this month's trading will only be settled, and no new purchases will be made. This announcement is made." The Social Affairs Bureau also replied to a letter from the bureau's council yesterday, saying: "Received and noted. It is stated that the original clients have been persuaded to automatically settle within the limits, and that the current flour market is active due to sales to other areas, causing prices to gradually rise. This is indeed the case and should be taken into consideration. The price limits for goods delivered in July, August, and September should be temporarily raised to 3.12 yuan, and the limits for October, November, and December should be 3.15 yuan, 3.18 yuan, and 3.21 yuan, respectively. All market prices must still not exceed the above limits. The request to cancel the price limits is temporarily denied." Therefore, all goods traded yesterday were bought and sold at the prices set by the Social Affairs Bureau.

Old Maid Yao Jinbao: One Fall Too Many 136

Yao Jinbao, an old maid from Kunshan, 39 years old, lived at No. 52 Caojiazhai, North Jisi Feier Road, West Shanghai. She vowed never to marry and made a living by chanting scriptures and praying for others. Unfortunately, around 9:00 PM the night before last, while returning home, she tripped and fell on the ground at the entrance of the Lu Xuezhai Yong'an Lane. Her neck hit a stone, and she bled profusely. Her neck suffered excessive impact, causing her to lose consciousness and die on the spot. Because there were few pedestrians in the area, it was not until yesterday morning that someone discovered her and reported it to the Caojiadu Public Security Bureau, which then reported it to the local court. The court sent Prosecutor Kong to the scene at around 10:00 AM to examine the body. It was confirmed that Yao Jinbao had fallen and injured her head, which caused her death. Neighbors in the area contributed money to provide for her burial.

Mr. Sheng, a paper merchant from Ningbo, resided at No. 4 Wuben Lane, An Najin Road, French Concession. Letters to the Editor 144

Having read today's report in your esteemed newspaper, on page 4, in the Wupu News column, there is a case of bandits robbing. The victim, Gu Yaosheng, was shot by robbers, injuring his left leg. The time of the incident and the circumstances of the robbery are inconsistent with the facts. It has been found that our office has already summoned the victim, Gu Yaosheng, for questioning. According to his statement, "Today at 3:10 PM, two robbers broke into the Gu Yaosheng Garden owned by me one after another, searching and robbing $18 in banknotes and $2 in silver coins. When leaving, they stabbed my left leg and both hands with a small kitchen knife. After escaping eastward, I went directly to the Red Cross Hospital for treatment. The robbers did not carry guns," etc. Accordingly, we are writing to request correction. Respectfully addressed to the Shenbao Newspaper Office, the Xujiahui Police Station of the Caojiadu Branch of the Public Security Bureau. Sincerely, July 18. Having read today's report in your esteemed newspaper, there is a news item about a British sailor beating a rickshaw puller to death. The facts are different. The points that should be corrected are as follows: (1) Your newspaper reported that Chen Huizhang died from a skull fracture after being hit in the head by a drunken British sailor. In fact, the British sailor was not drunk. After the incident, the reports in various newspapers did not mention drunkenness either. (2) The statement that the deceased's family, Chen Zhangshi, entrusted the Shanghai Rickshaw Mutual Aid Society to "negotiate for compensation" has been investigated. Yesterday afternoon, colleagues from our association personally went to the society to inquire. At that time, Mr. Xu Jieli, an executive of the society, replied that this mediation was not based on the initiative of the Rickshaw Mutual Aid Society, but rather he acted in his personal capacity to mediate and settle the case for 500 yuan. (3) The statement that the perpetrator in the case has left Shanghai with the warship is not accurate. The sailor was detained by the Public Works Department after the incident on the morning of the 8th of this month, and the procurator of the court strictly ordered the police to handle the case according to the law. The newspaper's casual statement is an inaccurate rumor. (4) It has been found that the representatives who went to the association yesterday afternoon were representatives and lawyers from the Jianghuai Compatriot Support Association for the Case of the British Sailor's Brutal Murder of Chen Huizhang, not representatives of the Jianghuai Compatriot Association. (5) Regarding the negotiation results, the representatives raised a "protest" because they did not pay attention to the entire national issue. Based on the above facts, there are many discrepancies, and it concerns the entire national system of China, so it cannot be confused with untruthful rumors. Therefore, we specially request your newspaper to make corrections and pray that the original letter will be published. Respectfully addressed to the chief editor of the Shenbao Newspaper Office. Sincerely, the Support Association for the Case of the British Sailor's Brutal Murder of Chen Huizhang, July 18, 1936.

It is said that the general association stipulates that county and city reviews should be held once a year. The organizational outline for the Jiangsu Provincial Scout Participation in the Second National Jamboree and Grand Review Committee was passed. The previous regulations of the Department of Education regarding subsidies for county scouts participating in district and provincial reviews are difficult to implement. It is requested that the Department of Education re-divide and set the subsidy amount according to the number of troops and the distance of the journey. Chen Bangcai and Zhu Chongming were additionally hired as trainers and members of the training camp committee in this province.
